\section{Preliminaries}\label{sec:prem}


\subsection{Tree formalism}	
\label{SUB:tree}





\begin{definition}
\label{DEF:tree}
\rm 
A \emph{binary tree} $\TT$ is a partially ordered set (with partial order $\le$) satisfying the following properties:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] $\TT$ has a unique minimal element called the \textit{root node} labelled by $\emptyset$ (i.e., $\emptyset \le a$ for all $a \in \TT$). 

\smallskip 
\item[(ii)] Given $a\in \TT\setminus \{ \emptyset \}$, 
there exists a unique $b \in \TT$ such that: $b\ne a$, $b \le a$, and $b \le c \le a$ implies $c\in\{a,b\}$. In that case, we say that $b$ is the \textit{parent} of $a$ and $a$ is a \textit{child} of $b$. 

\smallskip 
\item[(iii)] A node $a\in \TT$ is called \textit{terminal} or a \textit{leaf} if it has no children. A \textit{non-terminal node} or a \textit{parent} $a\in\TT$ is a node with exactly two children, one called \textit{left child} and the other \textit{right child}.\footnote{Introducing the notation of left and right children of a node  reflects the lack of ambiguity in the usual planar representation of binary trees.}  
We write $\TT^0, \TT^\infty$ for the sets of parent and terminal nodes of $\TT$, respectively.  Note that $\TT$ is the disjoint union of $\TT^0$ and $\TT^\infty$. 

\smallskip 
\item[(iv)]
Each node in $\TT$ is labelled with a word in the following way: the root node has word~$\emptyset$; and for a given parent node $a\in \TT^0$, its left and right children have labels $a1$ and $a2$,  obtained by concatenating $1$ or $2$ to the right of $a$, respectively. Note that children of the root node have labels 1 and 2. 


\end{enumerate}



\noi
We interchangeably use $\TT$ to denote the representation of the tree as a finite connected graph and to denote the set of words used to label its nodes. Note that the latter is also a partially ordered set, with words $a,b$ satisfying $a\le b$ if there exists a word $c$ such that $b = ac$. 



\end{definition}


Given $j\in\N$, we use the notation $\Tr_j$ to denote the family of all binary trees
with $j$ non-terminal nodes, which we call the $j$-th generation of trees. From Definition~\ref{DEF:tree}, it follows that 
\begin{align}
| \TT^0 |  = j \quad \text{and} \quad |\TT^\infty| = j+1.
\end{align}


\noi
It is not difficult to see that the number of distinct trees in $\Tr_j$ is given by the $j$-th Catalan number
\begin{align}\label{eq:catalan}
| \Tr_j | = \frac{1}{j+1} \binom{2j}{j}  = \frac{(2j)!}{(j+1)! j !}.
\end{align}
In particular, the first 3 generations of trees are succintly written below, identified by their graphs:
\begin{align*}
\Tr_1 & = \big\{ \<1> \big\}, \\
\Tr_2 & = \left\{ \<21>, \<22> \right\}, \\
\Tr_3 &  = \left\{ \<31>, \<32>, \<33>, \<34>, \<35> \right\}.
\end{align*}
Similarly, we can represent the trees above by the following partially ordered sets of words used to label their nodes (as per Definition \ref{DEF:tree}(iv)):
\begin{align}
\<1> 
&
= \{\emptyset\}
, 
\\
\<21>
&
=
\{ \emptyset, 1 ,2, 11,12  \}
, 
\\
\<22>
&
=
\{\emptyset, 1,2, 21,22\}
, 
\\
\<31>
&
= 
\{
\emptyset, 1,2, 11,12, 111, 112
\}
, \ldots
\end{align}




\smallskip








For readibility, we will reserve the symbols $\bul$, $\star$, $\circ$, and $\ast$ to denote nodes in a tree and their respective associated word. 
Next, we introduce some additional notation to identify different nodes in a tree. 


\begin{definition}\rm
\label{DEF:tree2}
Let $\TT$ be a binary tree in the sense of Definition~\ref{DEF:tree} and 
$\bul, \star$ be two nodes in $\TT$. 

\begin{enumerate}



\smallskip
\item[(i)]
If $\bul \in \TT\setminus \{ \emptyset\}$, we write $\pb(\bul)$ to denote the \emph{parent node} of $\bul$. If \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\pb(\star)\neq \emptyser$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\pb(\bul)\neq \emptyset$}\DIFaddend , we write $\gb(\bul)=\pb(\pb(\bul))$.

\smallskip
\item[(ii)] 
If $\bul, \star\in \TT \setminus\{ \emptyset \}$ are distinct and share the same parent, they are called \textit{siblings}. We write $\sbf(\bul)$ for the sibling of $\bul$. 

\smallskip
\item[(iii)] 
Given $\bul\in \TT^0$, we say $\bul$ is a \textit{final parent} if its children $\bul1, \bul2 \in \TT^\infty$. The set of final parents is denoted by $\TT^{0,\ff}$.


\end{enumerate}



\end{definition}


\begin{remark}\rm 
Note that from Definition~\ref{DEF:tree}, the maps $\pb, \sbf$, for the parent and sibling of a given node, are well-defined in their respective domains, since if either the parent or sibling node exists, it is unique. 

\end{remark}





We next introduce concatenation and subtraction of trees. 


\begin{definition} 
\label{DEF:tree3}
\rm

Let $\TT$ be a binary tree in the sense of Definition~\ref{DEF:tree}. 


\begin{enumerate}




\smallskip
\item[(i)] (Concatenation)  
Given $ \star \in \TT^\infty$, we define
$$
\TT \overset{\star}{\oplus} \<1>
: = \TT \cup \{\star1, \star2\}
$$
as the result of adding the children $\star1,\star2$ of $\star$ to the tree $\TT$. 
Note that this operation now makes $\star$ a final parent in the tree $\TT \overset{\star}{\oplus} \<1>$. 




\smallskip
\item[(ii)] (Subtraction) 
Given a final parent $\star  \in \TT^{0,\ff}$, we define the tree
$$
\TT \overset{\star }{\ominus } \<1>
: = \TT \setminus \{ \star1, \star2  \}
$$
as the result of eliminating the children $\star1, \star2$ of $\star$
from $\TT$. Note that $\star$ becomes a terminal node in the new tree $\TT \overset{\star}{\ominus } \<1>$. 
More generally, given $C\subseteq \TT^{0,f}$, we define
\begin{align}
\label{treeSubtr}
\TT \overset{C}{\ominus} \<1> : =
 \bigcap_{\star \in C} ( \TT \overset{\star}{\ominus}  \<1>)
= \bigcap_{\star\in C} (\TT \setminus \{\star1,\star2\})
= \TT \setminus \Big( \bigcup_{\star\in C} \{\star1,\star2\} \Big), 
\end{align}
which corresponds to the set where all the children of the final parents $\star\in C$ have been removed from the tree.


\end{enumerate}



\end{definition}



The tree structure defined above and its word-labelling will help in keeping track of the nonlinear terms appearing in \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{our }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the }\DIFaddend normal form reduction \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{procedure. Namely, after an }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{performed in Subsection~\ref{sec:nfe}. There, after a }\DIFaddend differentiation-by-parts step \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{in time}\DIFaddend , a time derivative falls on a $v$-factor \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{as in \eqref{NF00}, after which we use equation \eqref{dtv} to replace it }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and is replaced, via the equation for $\dt \widehat v$, }\DIFaddend by a quadratic term, generating a \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{higher degree }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{higher-degree }\DIFaddend nonlinear contribution. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We can then use binary trees to label }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Binary trees provide a natural bookkeeping for }\DIFaddend the frequencies of the corresponding factors, in the following way.


\begin{definition}\rm 

Let $j\in\N$ and $\TT \in \Tr_j$. 

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(i)] (Index function) 
We define the index function $\vec\xi : \TT\to \CC^\TT$ such that $\vec\xi = (\xi_\bul)_{\bul\in\TT}$, where
\begin{align}
\label{parent}
\xi_\bul = \xi_{\bul1} + \xi_{\bul2}, \quad \bul\in \TT^0,
\end{align}
and $\bul1$ and $\bul2$ denote the children of $\bul$. Moreover, we define the set $\G(\TT)$ as the set of convolution relations on the tree $\TT$:
\begin{align}
\label{Gamma}
\G(\TT) : = \big\{ \vec\xi \in \CC^\TT: \ \xi_\bul = \xi_{\bul1} + \xi_{\bul2}, \ \bul \in \TT^0 \big\}. 
\end{align}


\smallskip

\item[(ii)] (Zero-energy phase function) 
We use \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\Psi(\TT)$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\Psi_0(\TT)$ }\DIFaddend to denote the \textit{zero-energy phase function} associated with the tree $\TT$, given by
\begin{align}
\label{psi0-tree}
\Psi_0(\TT)
:=
\Re\left(- \xi^3 + \sum_{\bul\in \TT^\infty} \xi_\bul^3\right)
\end{align}
where $\TT^\infty$ denotes the set of leaves of $\TT$. 


Given a parent node $\star\in\TT^0$, we also introduce the partial zero-energy phase function for the tree $\cherry{\star}{}{}=\{\star, \star1, \star2\}$:
\begin{align}
\label{psi-circ}
\Psi_0(\star) = \Psi_0(\cherry{\star}{}{}) : = - \xi^3_\star + \xi^3_{\star1} + \xi^3_{\star2}. 
\end{align}
Note that the following additivity property holds for $\Psi$:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:additivity}
\Psi_0(\TT) = \sum_{\star \in \TT^0} \Psi_0(\star). 
\end{equation}
\item[(iii)] (Energy phase function) Given a binary tree $\TT$, we also define the \textit{energy phase function} as
\begin{align}
\label{psiE-tree}
\Psi_E(\TT)
:=
-\Re\left(- \frac{\xi^3}{|\xi|^2} + \sum_{\bul\in \TT^\infty} \frac{\xi_\bul^3}{|\xi_\bul|^2}\right).
\end{align}
The partial energy phase function is given as
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{psi-circ}
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi_E(\star) = \Psi_E(\cherry{\star}{}{}).
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align}
\label{psi-circ-E}
\Psi_E(\star) = \Psi_E(\cherry{\star}{}{}).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\item[(iv)] (Phase function) For a fixed binary tree $\TT$, the (total) phase function is then defined as
\begin{equation}
\Psi(\TT)=\Psi_0(\TT) + E \Psi_E(\TT).
\end{equation}
Given $\star\in \TT^0$, we write
$$
\Psi(\star)=\Psi_0(\star) + E \Psi_E(\star)
$$
\item[(v)] 
Lastly, for $\star\in \TT^0$, we define the multiplier $K_\star$ given by
\begin{equation}
\label{Kmul}
K_{\star} := \frac{\xi_{\star1}\cdot\xi_{\star2}}{|\xi_{\star1}|^2|\xi_{\star2}|^2},
\end{equation}
where $\xi_{\star1}\cdot\xi_{\star2}$ is the $\R^2$ inner product.


\end{enumerate}




\end{definition}

To describe the infinite normal form reduction, we introduce a correspondence between binary trees and oscillatory integrals. 
Given $j\in\N$, a binary tree $\TT \in \Tr_j$, a multiplier $m:\CC^{\TT}\to \CC$ on $\TT$, and a
function $v: \R\times \CC \to\CC$, we define the associated integral term
\begin{equation}\label{eq:defiI}
\Ical(\TT, m; v)(t) :=   i \int_{\G(\TT)}
e^{it\Psi(\TT)}m(\vec{\xi})
\prod_{\bul\in \TT^\infty}  \ft v_\bul (t) d\vec{\xi},
\end{equation}
where 
we use the short-hand notation  $\ft v_\bul(t) := \ft v(t,\xi_\bul)$ for a label $\bul$. 

\subsection{Deriving the normal form equation}\label{sec:nfe}

Using the tree formalism in Subsection~\ref{SUB:tree}, we now derive the normal form equation which we shall use.
We apply a normal form reduction in the form of ``differentiation-by-parts" as in \cite{bit}, only in a problematic region where we cannot show the nonlinear estimate at low regularity.
In particular, we consider the following sets $A$ and $A^c = \G({\<1>}) \setminus A$: 
\begin{align}
\label{A}\begin{split} 
A & := \big\{ (\xi_{1}, \xi_{2}) \in \R^2: \ \xi_{1}+ \xi_{2} = \xi, \  |\xi_{1}| \lor  |\xi_{2}| \le 1/\delta  \big\}, \\
A^c & := \big\{ (\xi_{1}, \xi_2) \in \R^2: \ \xi_{1}+ \xi_{2} = \xi,  \ |\xi_{1}| \lor |\xi_{2}| \ge 1/\delta  \big\}, 
\end{split}
\end{align}

where $A^c$ denotes the bad region where we perform a reduction. 


Using the tree-indexing in Subsection~\ref{SUB:tree} and the notations in \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{psi-tree}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\eqref{psi0-tree}}\DIFaddend , \eqref{psi-circ}, and \eqref{Kmul}, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we rewrite \eqref{dtv} as follows}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the equation satisfied by $v=\F_z(U(-t)u)$, in the interaction representation, can be written as follows:
}\DIFaddend \begin{align}
\label{duhamel2}
\dt\ft v(t) =  i \int_{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2} e^{it \Psi(\<1>)}  K \Psi_0(\<1>)   (\widehat{v}_{1} \widehat{v}_{2}) (t)
d\xi_{1}.
\end{align}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\joao{There are multiplicative terms in front of the integral, but I'm supposing they won't matter in the end (?)}
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{(Absolute multiplicative constants in front of the integral have been absorbed into the multiplier; see the discussion preceding~\eqref{eq:NV2}.)
}\DIFaddend Then, splitting the region of integration into $A\cup A^c$ as in \eqref{A}, we may write \eqref{duhamel2} as 
\begin{align}
\dt\ft v
&
= 
\Ical\big( \<1>, \ind_A K \Psi_0(\<1>); v 
\big)
+ \Ical\big( \<1>, \ind_{A^c} K \Psi_0(\<1>) ;v 
\big)
\label{NFE000}
\end{align}
where $\Ical$ is as in \eqref{eq:defiI}. In order to perform a differentiation-by-parts in time on the $\MM$-term restricted to the bad region $A^c$, we need to make the total phase $\Psi(\<1>)$ appear. Hence, we simply recall that 
\[
\Psi(\<1>) = \Psi_0(\<1>) + E \Psi_E (\<1>).
\]
This allows us to write 
\begin{align}
\dt\ft v
&
= 
\Ical\big( \<1>, \ind_A K \Psi_0(\<1>); v 
\big)
+ \Ical\big( \<1>, \ind_{A^c} K \Psi (\<1>) ;v 
\big)
\\
& - \Ical \big(\<1>, E \cdot K \cdot \Psi_E(\<1>);v\big) + \Ical \big(\<1>, \ind_A K \cdot E \cdot \Psi_E(\<1>); v\big) 
\\
& 
= \Ical \big(\<1>, \ind_A K \Psi_0(\<1>) - \ind_{A^c} K \cdot E \cdot \Psi_E(\<1>);v\big) + \Ical(\<1>, \ind_{A^c} K \Psi(\<1>);v) 
\\
& 
=: \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )] + \Ft_x[ \MM(\<1>; v) ].
\label{NFE001}
\end{align}
In order to move on with our development, we start by using the relation
$$
\dt\frac{e^{it\Psi(\<1>)}}{i\Psi(\<1>)}=e^{it\Psi(\<1>)},
$$ 
which allows us to perform the first differentiation-by-parts step in our chain. We obtain
\begin{align}
\label{NFE01}
\begin{split}
\dt\ft v(t)  
&=
\Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )] (t)
+ \dt\bigg[ \int_{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2} e^{it \Psi(\<1>)} 
[\ind_{A^c}
 K ] 
(\ft v_{1} \ft v_{2} )(t)
d\xi_{1} 
\bigg]
\\
&
\quad 
-
   \int_{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2} e^{it \Psi(\<1>)} 
[ \ind_{A^c} K ]
\partial_{t} (\ft v_{1} \ft v_{2} )(t)
d\xi_{1} 
\\
& =
\Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )] (t)
+  \dt\bigg[ \int_{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2} e^{it \Psi(\<1>)} 
[\ind_{A^c}
 K ] 
(\ft v_{1} \ft v_{2} )(t)
d\xi_{1} 
\bigg]
\\
&
\quad 
- i
 \int_{\substack{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2 \\ \xi_1 = \xi_{11}+ \xi_{12}  }} \exp\Big(it \Psi(\<21>) \Big)
[ \ind_{A^c} K K_1 \Psi_0(1) ]
 (\ft v_{11} \ft v_{12} \ft v_2 )(t)
d\xi_{1} d\xi_{11} 
\\
&
\quad 
-i  \int_{\substack{\xi = \xi_1 + \xi_2 \\ \xi_2 = \xi_{21}+ \xi_{22}  }} \exp\Big(it \Psi(\<22>) \Big)
[ \ind_{A^c} K K_2 \Psi_0(2) ]
 (\ft v_{1} \ft v_{21} \ft v_{22} )(t)
d\xi_{1} d\xi_{21}
\end{split}
\end{align}
where we replaced $\dt \ft v_j$ by \eqref{duhamel2} to obtain the last equality. This can be rewritten as
\begin{align}
\label{NFE00}
\begin{split}
\dt\ft v 
&
=
 \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )] 
+ 
\dt\Ical \big( \<1>,  - i \ind_{A^c} K; v \big) 
\\
&
\quad 
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c} KK_1\Psi_0(1) ; v  \Big) 
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c} KK_2\Psi_0(2) ; v  \Big) 
. 
\end{split}
\end{align}






In order to iterate the procedure taking \eqref{duhamel2} into \eqref{NFE00}, we use the following result. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{This }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{It }\DIFaddend provides a systematic way to perform a normal form reduction on integral terms of the form $\Ical$ in \eqref{eq:defiI}, which \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{per se }\DIFdelend translates to an operation on trees (based on tree concatenation as defined in Definition~\ref{DEF:tree3}~(ii)) and suitable modifications of the multipliers. We refer the reader to the companion \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{paper CITE for its proof- which, in spite of not being identical, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{KdV paper~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
for the proof, which }\DIFaddend works in the exact same fashion in our \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{context}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{setting}\DIFaddend .


\begin{lemma}[Differentiation-by-parts on trees]
\label{LEM:IBP}
Let $j\in\N$, $\TT\in\Tr_j$, $m: \R^{\TT}\to \mathbb{C}$ a multiplier on $\TT$,
and $v$ be a smooth function such that $\ft v$ satisfies \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{dtv}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\eqref{duhamel2}}\DIFaddend . Then, the following identity holds
\begin{align}\label{IBP}
\begin{split}
\Ical (\TT,m; v)
= \dt \Ical \Big(\TT,\frac{m}{ i \Psi(\TT)} ; v \Big)
+ \sum_{\star \in \TT^\infty} \Ical 
\Big(\TT \overset{\star}{\oplus} \<1>
, - K_\star \Psi_0(\star) \frac{m}{\Psi(\TT)} ; v \Big)
,
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $\Ical$ is the integral functional in \eqref{eq:defiI}, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\TT \overset{\star}{\oplus} \<1> $ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\TT \overset{\star}{\oplus} \<1>$ }\DIFaddend denotes tree concatenation at the final node $\star\in \TT^\infty$ as in Definition~\ref{DEF:tree3}~(ii), and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\Psi(\TT), \Psi(\star),  K_\star$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\Psi(\TT)$, $\Psi(\star)$, $K_\star$ }\DIFaddend are as in \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{psi-tree}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\eqref{psi0-tree}}\DIFaddend , \eqref{psi-circ}, and \eqref{Kmul}.

\end{lemma}



\noi
As in \eqref{NFE01}, we split each region of frequency integration between a good and a bad set, and only perform a differentiation-by-parts when restricted to the latter. Generalizing the definition of $A, A^c$ in \eqref{A}, given a tree $\TT$ and a parent node $\bul \in \TT^0$, we define the analogous sets $A_\bul$ and $A_\bul^c$ as
\begin{align}
A_\bul& 
:=
 \big\{ (\xi_{\bul1}, \xi_{\bul2}) \in \R^2: \ \xi_\bul =
\xi_{\bul1}
+ \xi_{\bul2}, \ |\xi_{\bul1}| \lor  |\xi_{\bul2}|  \le 1/\delta 
 \} , \\
A_\bul^c & := \big\{ (\xi_{\bul1}, \xi_{\bul2}) \in \R^2: \ \xi_\bul =
\xi_{\bul1} +
\xi_{\bul2},\
|\xi_{\bul1}| \lor |\xi_{\bul2}| \ge 1/\delta \big\} 
.
\label{defA}
\end{align}
Note that, when $\bul = \emptyset$ is the root node, $A_\bul =A$ as in \eqref{A}. 
We will often omit the dependence on the children frequencies $\xi_{\bul 1}, \xi_{\bul2}$ of $\xi_\bul$, and use the short-hand notation $\ind_{A_\bul}=\ind_{A_\bul} (\xi_{\bul1},\xi_{\bul2})$.
%Moreover, we note the following relation between the frequencies in the sets in \eqref{defA}:
%\begin{align}
%\label{defA2}
%\begin{split}
%(\xi_{\bul1}, \xi_{\bul2}) \in A_\bul 
%&
%\implies 1/\delta \le (|\xi_{\bul1}| \lor |\xi_{\bul2}|) \sim |\xi_\bul| \sim \big| | \xi_{\bul1}| - |\xi_{\bul2}| \big|
%,
%\\
%(\xi_{\bul1}, \xi_{\bul2}) \in A_\bul^{c} 
%&
%\implies (1/\delta) \lor  |\xi_{\bul}|  \les |\xi_{\bul1}| \sim |\xi_{\bul2}|
%.
%\end{split}
%\end{align}


Returning to \eqref{NFE00}, we continue to derive the second iteration of the normal form equation.
Unlike the first normal form reduction from equation \eqref{duhamel2} to \eqref{NFE00}, where we split the integral term into $A$ and $A^c$ (see \eqref{A}) and differentiate-by-parts in the latter region, we now have an additional step, which we describe in the following. Considering the two last terms in \eqref{NFE00}, we first split their regions of integration $(\xi_{\bul1}, \xi_{\bul2}) \in A_\bul \cup A_\bul^c$, where $\bul = 1,2$, respectively:
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{NFE001}
%DIFDELCMD < \dt\ft v
%DIFDELCMD < &
%DIFDELCMD < = 
%DIFDELCMD <  \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )]  
%DIFDELCMD < + 
%DIFDELCMD < \dt \Ical \big( \<1>, -i  \ind_{A^c} K; v \big)
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &
%DIFDELCMD < \quad 
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1} KK_1\Psi_0(1) ; v  \Big)  
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1^c} KK_1\Psi_0(1) ; v  \Big) 
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &
%DIFDELCMD < \quad 
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2} KK_2\Psi_0(2) ; v  \Big) 
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2^c} KK_2\Psi_0(2) ; v  \Big) .
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align}
\label{NFE001b}
\dt\ft v
&
= 
 \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )]  
+ 
\dt \Ical \big( \<1>, -i  \ind_{A^c} K; v \big)
\\
&
\quad 
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1} KK_1\Psi_0(1) ; v  \Big)  
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1^c} KK_1\Psi_0(1) ; v  \Big) 
\\
&
\quad 
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2} KK_2\Psi_0(2) ; v  \Big) 
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2^c} KK_2\Psi_0(2) ; v  \Big) .
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
As a first preparatory step, we add and subtract the `energy' terms, in order to complete the phases in the last couple of lines above. Indeed, we first write 
\[
\Psi(\star) = \big( \Psi_0(\star) + E \cdot \Psi_E (\star) \big) - E \cdot \Psi_E(\star),
\]
which allows us to write 
\begin{align}
\label{NFE0011}
\dt\ft v
&
= 
 \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )]  
+ 
\dt \Ical \big( \<1>, -i  \ind_{A^c} K; v \big)
\\
&
\quad 
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, K K_1 \ind_{A^c} \cdot \left( E \ind_{A_1^c}  \Psi_E(1) - \ind_{A_1} \Psi_0(1) \right) ; v  \Big)  
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1^c} KK_1\Psi(1) ; v  \Big) 
\\
&
\quad 
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, KK_2 \ind_{A^c} \left( E \ind_{A_2^c} \Psi_E(2) - \ind_{A_2} \Psi_0(2)\right) ; v  \Big) 
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2^c} KK_2\Psi(2) ; v  \Big). 
\end{align}

As before, we keep the integral contributions which either come from a `lower-order' \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{/}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{or }\DIFaddend energy term, or which are localized to a ``good set" $A_\bul$. Regarding the contributions restricted to $A_\bul^c$ for all $\bul\in \TT^0$, despite the restriction to the ``bad regions'', we will keep a suitable part of these terms before performing another differentiation-by-parts. In particular, by using the additivity of the phase $\Psi$ in \eqref{eq:additivity}, we write
\begin{align}
\Psi(\star) 
= \big[ \Psi(\star) + \Psi(\<1>) \big]- \Psi(\<1>) 
=
\Psi(\TT) - \Psi(\<1>),
\quad (\star, \TT)\in \left\{ (1, \<21>) , (2, \<22>) \right\},
\end{align}
and keep the contributions with partial phase $-\Psi(\<1>)$, only differentiating-by-parts the terms with total phase $\Psi(\TT)$. Then, from \eqref{NFE001}, we obtain the second iteration of the normal form equation
\begin{align}
\dt\ft v
&
= 
 \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )] 
+ 
\dt \Ical \big( \<1>, - i  \ind_{A^c} K; v \big)
\\
&
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>,  K K_1 \ind_{A^c} \cdot \left( \ind_{A_1^c} \Psi(\<1>) + E \ind_{A_1^c}  \Psi_E(1) - \ind_{A_1} \Psi_0(1) \right); v  \Big) 
\\
&
+
\Ical \Big( \<21>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_1^c} KK_1\Psi(\<21>) ; v  \Big) 
\\
&
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, KK_2 \ind_{A^c} \left( \ind_{A_2^c} \Psi(\<1>) + E \ind_{A_2^c} \Psi_E(2) - \ind_{A_2} \Psi_0(2)\right) ; v  \Big) 
\\
&
+
\Ical \Big( \<22>, - \ind_{A^c \cap A_2^c} KK_2\Psi(\<22>) ; v  \Big) 
\\
&
= : 
 \Ft_x[ \NN ( \<1>; v )]  
+ 
 \Ft_x[ 
\BB(\<1>;v)
] 
\\
&
\quad 
+ 
 \Ft_x[ 
\NN(\<21>; v )
] 
+
 \Ft_x[ 
\MM(\<21>; v )
] 
+
 \Ft_x[ 
\NN(\<22>; v)
]  
+
 \Ft_x[ 
\MM(\<22>;v)
]  
.
\label{NFE002}
\end{align}
In the Duhamel expansion of $v$, based on \eqref{NFE002}, $\NN$ corresponds to time-integral terms, $\BB$ to boundary terms, and $\MM$ are remainders, to which we apply \eqref{IBP} at the next step. Thus, in the following, we refer to them as integral terms, boundary terms, and remainders, respectively.



In the following iterations of the normal form equation, as in \eqref{NFE00} and \eqref{NFE002}, for each tree $\TT$, we want to have a unique integral term $\NN(\TT)$ and boundary term $\BB(\TT)$, 
where this must encode all the possible ways of arriving at such a tree structure. 
From Lemma~\ref{LEM:IBP}, we note that given a tree $\TT \in \Tr_j$ for $j\ge2$, after differentiation-by-parts, the resulting contributions associated with the tree $\TT$ can come from any term of the form $\Ical(\TT \overset{\star}{\ominus} \<1>)$ where $\star \in \TT^{0, \ff}$, i.e., that the children of $\star$ are leaves in $\TT$. Consequently, in the following, we need to perform differentiation-by-parts on the remainder terms $\MM(\TT)$ simultaneously and combine any contributions associated with the same tree before preparing the integral terms to be kept and those which will be differentiated in the following step. 

The following result provides a systematic way of repeating the process described above, with an explicit description of the contributions and multipliers involved at each finite normal form equation. 
We note that we see one boundary term and an integral term for each tree of a given generation $\Tr_j$, with the complexity of the contributions being encoded in the corresponding multipliers.








\begin{proposition}
\label{PRO:NFE}
Let $J\in\N$, $u$ be a smooth solution to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{kdv}, and $v$ as in \eqref{inter} be a solution to \eqref{dtv}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\eqref{eq:NV}, and $v=\F_z(U(-t)u)$ be the corresponding solution to \eqref{duhamel2}}\DIFaddend .
Then, 
the $J$-th normal form equation for $v$ is given by
\begin{align}
\label{NFE1}
\dt v=
\sum_{j=1}^{J-1} \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \BB(\TT; v) 
+ \sum_{j=1}^{J} \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \NN(\TT; v) 
+ \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_{J}}
\MM(\TT; v),
\end{align}
where the operators are defined via their spatial Fourier transforms
\begin{align}
\label{NFE1a}
\begin{split}
\Ft_x [\BB(\TT;v)]  & = \dt\Ical(\TT, - i \mulB(\TT); v),\\
\Ft_x [\NN(\TT;v)]  & = \Ical(\TT, \mul(\TT) ; v  ), \\
\Ft_x [\MM(\TT;v)] & = \Ical(\TT, \Psi(\TT)\mulB(\TT); v),
\end{split}
\end{align}

\noi
with $\Ical(\TT, m; v)$ as in \eqref{eq:defiI}.
Moreover,
the multipliers $\mul(\TT)$ and $\mulB(\TT)$ for $\TT\in \Tr_j$ are given by
\begin{align}
\label{NFE0b}
\begin{split}
\mulB(\TT)
& =  (-1)^{j+1}  \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0}  \ind_{A^c_{\bul}} K_\bul
,
\\
\mul(\TT) & =  (-1)^{j+1} \bigg(\prod_{\bul \in \TT^0} K_\bul \bigg) \bigg\{  \sum_{\star \in \TT^{0,f}}
\left(\ind_{A_{\star}} \Psi_0(\star) - \ind_{A_{\star}^c} E\Psi_E(\star)\right)\bigg(\prod_{\substack{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}
}} \ind_{A^c_{\bul}} \bigg)\\
&
\hspace{4cm}
-
\bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0} \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg)
\sum_{\star\in \TT^0 \setminus \TT^{0,\ff}} \Psi(\star)
 \bigg\},
\end{split}
\end{align}
where $K_\bul$ and $\Psi(\star)$ are as in \eqref{Kmul} and \eqref{psi-circ}. 

\end{proposition}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Motivated by Proposition\ref{PRO:NFE}, we can formally take the limit $J\to \infty$ to derive the infinite normal form equation for $v$:
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{NFE}
%DIFDELCMD < \dt v= \sum_{j=1}^{\infty} \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \left(\NN(\TT;v) +
%DIFDELCMD < \BB(\TT;v) \right)
%DIFDELCMD < ,
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend %DIF >  =====================================================================
%DIF >  gauge.tex --- Subsection: change of variables and gauged equation.
%DIF >  Revision log (condensed):
%DIF >    Pass 1: catalogued paragraphs overlapping with [chcora, Sec. 2.3].
%DIF >    Pass 2: rewrote the roadmap and the proof of LEM:wbd as a self-
%DIF >      contained one-line multiplier identity, in prose distinct from KdV.
%DIF >    Pass 3: replaced the re-derivation of the inclusion-exclusion by an
%DIF >      explicit citation of [chcora, Lemma 2.10, Steps 1-2]; only the
%DIF >      gfrak_E piece, which is NV-specific, is spelled out in full.
%DIF >  =====================================================================
\DIFaddbegin 


\DIFadd{Taking $J\to\infty$ in Proposition~\ref{PRO:NFE} yields, at the formal level, the }\emph{\DIFadd{infinite normal form equation}}
\begin{align}
\label{NFE}
\dt v= \sum_{j=1}^{\infty} \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \left(\NN(\TT;v) + \BB(\TT;v) \right),
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
with $\NN(\TT;v)$ and $\BB(\TT;v)$ as in \eqref{NFE1a}.
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Our next step is then a }\emph{\DIFdel{change-of-variables}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{procedure, which is intended to eliminate the boundary terms stemming from \eqref{NFE}. We derive the modified normal form equation for the new variable $w$, which is related to $v$ by a nonlinear transformation. In particular, the equation for $w$ (see \eqref{w2})includes no boundary terms and all the integral terms can be estimated via frequency-restricted estimates}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin 

\DIFadd{Our route from~\eqref{NFE} to the gauged equation has three stages. First, a single nonlinear substitution $v\mapsto w$ is engineered to absorb the quadratic boundary term in~\eqref{NFE}; the surprising fact is that the same substitution eliminates }\emph{\DIFadd{every}} \DIFadd{boundary term via an algebraic identity (Lemma~\ref{LEM:wbd}). Second, an analogous cancellation on the nonlinear side reduces the surviving multipliers to five families, which we tabulate (Lemma~\ref{LEM:wint}). Third, the interaction representation $z(t):=U(-t)w(t)$ recasts the system as the gauged Novikov--Veselov equation~\eqref{z1}. The algebra runs in close parallel with~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, with one structural novelty: alongside the dispersive phase $\Psi_0$, the energy phase $E\Psi_E$ contributes its own family of multipliers (Type~$\III$), so the inclusion-exclusion bookkeeping is carried out on the pair $(\Psi_0,E\Psi_E)$ rather than on a single phase}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Before defining our change of variables, we introduce a multilinear version of the functional }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \subsubsection*{\DIFadd{The multilinear functional and the change of variables}}

\DIFadd{It will be convenient to evaluate }\DIFaddend $\Ical$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in \eqref{eq:defiI} .
Let $j\in \N$ and $\TT\in \Tr_j$. Consider }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from~\eqref{eq:defiI} at distinct inputs. Fix $j\in\N$ and $\TT\in\Tr_j$, and order }\DIFaddend the $j+1$ leaves of $\TT$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{ordered with respect to their words:
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{lexic}
%DIFDELCMD < \bul_1\le \bul_2\le \dots \le \bul_{j+1}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{lexicographically by their words,
}\begin{align}
\label{lexic}
\bul_1\le \bul_2\le \dots \le \bul_{j+1},
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Graphically,
in a
planar representation of the tree, this corresponds to ordering the leaves of
$\TT$ from left to right. Given space-time functions $v_1,\dots, v_{j+1}: \R \times \R \to \R$, we
define the multilinear operator
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:defiImulti}
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical(\TT, m; v_1,\dots,v_{j+1}) (t)=i
%DIFDELCMD < \int_{\Gamma_\TT}
%DIFDELCMD < e^{it\Psi(\TT)}m(\vec{\xi}) \prod_{\ell
%DIFDELCMD < =1}^{j+1} \ft v_\l (t,\xi_{\bul_\ell}) d\vec{\xi}
%DIFDELCMD < .
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{i.e.\ left-to-right in any planar drawing. For arbitrary smooth $v_1,\dots,v_{j+1}:\R\times \R^2\to\R$, set
}\begin{equation}
\label{eq:defiImulti}
\Ical(\TT, m; v_1,\dots,v_{j+1}) (t)
= i \int_{\Gamma_\TT} e^{it\Psi(\TT)} m(\vec{\xi}) \prod_{\ell=1}^{j+1} \ft v_\l (t,\xi_{\bul_\ell})\, d\vec{\xi}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Note that
when $v_1 = \cdots = v_{j+1} = v$, the definition above agrees with that of$\Ical(\TT, m; v )$ in \eqref{eq:defiI}. Moreover, we define the multilinear analogues }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Specialising $v_1=\cdots=v_{j+1}=v$ recovers $\Ical(\TT, m; v)$ of~\eqref{eq:defiI}. The multilinear counterparts }\DIFaddend of $\BB(\TT)$ and $\NN(\TT)$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in \eqref{NFE1a} in Proposition~\ref{PRO:NFE} in the following natural way:
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}\Ft_x [\BB(\TT; v_1, \ldots, v_{j+1}) ]  &=
%DIFDELCMD < \dt\Ical (\TT,- i \mulB(\TT) ; v_1,\dots,v_{j+1}),\\
%DIFDELCMD < \Ft_x [\NN(\TT; v_1, \ldots, v_{j+1} ) ] 
%DIFDELCMD < &= 
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical(\TT,\mul(\TT) ; v_1, \ldots,
%DIFDELCMD < v_{j+1} )
%DIFDELCMD < .
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{from~\eqref{NFE1a} are then
}\begin{align*}
\Ft_x [\BB(\TT; v_1, \ldots, v_{j+1}) ]  &= \dt\Ical (\TT,- i \mulB(\TT) ; v_1,\dots,v_{j+1}),\\
\Ft_x [\NN(\TT; v_1, \ldots, v_{j+1} ) ]  &= \Ical(\TT,\mul(\TT) ; v_1, \ldots, v_{j+1} ).
\end{align*}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We now introduce our change of variables }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Define }\DIFaddend $v\mapsto w$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, defined via
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{w}
%DIFDELCMD < v 
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < w + \Ical(\<1>, - i \mulB(\<1>); w)
%DIFDELCMD < =:
%DIFDELCMD < w + \D[w, w]
%DIFDELCMD < ,
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{implicitly by
}\begin{align}
\label{w}
v = w + \Ical(\<1>, - i \mulB(\<1>); w) =: w + \D[w, w],
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{where }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with }\DIFaddend $\Ical$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{is as in\eqref{eq:defiI}. Then, we have
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{as in~\eqref{eq:defiI}. By design, $\partial_t\D[w,w]$ reproduces precisely the quadratic boundary contribution $\BB(\<1>;w)$, so
}\DIFaddend \begin{align}
\label{wa}
\dt v = \dt w + \BB(\<1>; w),
\end{align}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with }\DIFaddend $\BB$ as in\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{NFE1a} in 
Proposition~\ref{PRO:NFE}; see also \eqref{NFE002}.
Combining \eqref{wa} with the normal form equation \eqref{NFE}, andreplacing $v$ with the change of variables \eqref{w} , we obtain a closed equation for~$w$:
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \dt w & = -  \BB(\<1>;w) + \BB(\<1>;v) + \NN(\<1>;v)
%DIFDELCMD < + \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in\Tr_j} \Big( \NN(\TT; v)  +
%DIFDELCMD < \BB(\TT; v) 
%DIFDELCMD <  \Big) \nonumber\\
%DIFDELCMD < & = 
%DIFDELCMD <  \BB\big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w] \big) 
%DIFDELCMD < + \BB \big(\<1>; \D[w, w],w\big) 
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \BB\big(\<1>; \D[w,w], \D[w, w]\big) 
%DIFDELCMD <   \nonumber\\
%DIFDELCMD < & \qquad 
%DIFDELCMD < + \NN(\<1>; w ,w )  + \NN\big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w]\big) 
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \NN\big(\<1>; \D[w, w], w\big) 
%DIFDELCMD < + \NN\big(\<1>; \D[w, w],\D[w, w]\big) 
%DIFDELCMD <  \nonumber\\
%DIFDELCMD < & \qquad 
%DIFDELCMD < + \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} 
%DIFDELCMD < \Big( \NN\big(\TT; w+
%DIFDELCMD < \D[w, w]
%DIFDELCMD < \big) 
%DIFDELCMD < +  \BB\big(\TT; w + \D[w, w]\big) \Big).
%DIFDELCMD < \label{w1}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\eqref{NFE1a} (cf.~\eqref{NFE002}). Plugging~\eqref{wa} and~\eqref{w} into~\eqref{NFE} gives the closed equation
}\begin{align}
\dt w
& = -\BB(\<1>;w) + \BB(\<1>;v) + \NN(\<1>;v) + \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in\Tr_j} \Big( \NN(\TT; v)  + \BB(\TT; v) \Big) \nonumber \\
& =  \BB\big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w] \big) + \BB \big(\<1>; \D[w, w],w\big) + \BB\big(\<1>; \D[w,w], \D[w, w]\big) \nonumber\\
& \qquad + \NN(\<1>; w ,w )  + \NN\big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w]\big) + \NN\big(\<1>; \D[w, w], w\big) + \NN\big(\<1>; \D[w, w],\D[w, w]\big) \nonumber\\
& \qquad + \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \Big( \NN\big(\TT; w+ \D[w, w] \big) +  \BB\big(\TT; w + \D[w, w]\big) \Big).
\label{w1}
\end{align}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Note that unlike \eqref{NFE} for $v$, the equation in \eqref{w1} has multiple contributions with the same homogeneity }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Because $\D[w,w]$ is itself quadratic }\DIFaddend in $w$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{coming from operators $\BB$ and $\NN$ evaluated at different trees, 
since the operator $\D[w, w]$ has
two copies of $w$. 
It induces us naturally then to rewrite \eqref{w1} by combining terms with }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{expanding~\eqref{w1} produces, for each underlying tree, several terms of }\DIFaddend the same homogeneity \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in $w$ and associated with the same tree, moving the complexity to the corresponding multipliers . This process leads to a fundamental cancellation, since }\textit{\DIFdel{all the boundary terms cancel}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{, as shown in the following lemma}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{but supported on different colourings. Bundling such terms tree-by-tree shifts the combinatorial overhead into the multipliers and reveals a striking algebraic phenomenon: }\emph{\DIFadd{every}} \DIFadd{boundary term is annihilated}\DIFaddend .

\DIFaddbegin \subsubsection*{\DIFadd{The boundary cancellation}}

\DIFaddend \begin{lemma}
\label{LEM:wbd}
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend Let $j\in\N$, $\TT\in \Tr_j$, $\star \in \TT^{0,\ff}$, and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$w_1, \ldots, w_{j+1}: \R\times \R \to \R$ be any smoothfunctions. Moreover, consider the lexicographical ordering of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{let $w_1, \ldots, w_{j+1}: \R\times \R^2 \to \R$ be smooth. Order }\DIFaddend the leaves of $\TT$ as in\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend \eqref{lexic}, and let $1 \le k \le j$ be such that $(\bul_k, \bul_{k+1})$ are the children of $\star$ in $\TT$. Then
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we have 
}\DIFdelend \begin{align}
\label{wbd0}
\BB\big(\TT ; w_1, \ldots, w_{j+1} \big)
+ \BB\big(\TT\overset{\star}{\ominus} \<1>; w_1,  \ldots, w_{k-1} , \D[w_k,w_{k+1}] , w_{k+2}, \ldots,  w_{j+1} \big) \equiv 0.
\end{align}
Consequently, all the boundary terms in\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend \eqref{w1} vanish:
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{multline}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{wbd1}
%DIFDELCMD <   \BB \big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w] \big) 
%DIFDELCMD < + \BB\big(\<1>; \D[w, w],w\big) 
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < \BB\big(\<1>;\D[w, w], \D[w, w]\big)
%DIFDELCMD < + \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j}  \BB\big(\TT; w + \D[w, w]\big)  \equiv 0  .
%DIFDELCMD < \end{multline}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{multline}
\label{wbd1}
  \BB \big(\<1>; w, \D[w, w] \big)
+ \BB\big(\<1>; \D[w, w],w\big)
+ \BB\big(\<1>;\D[w, w], \D[w, w]\big)
\\
+ \sum_{j=2}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j}  \BB\big(\TT; w + \D[w, w]\big)  \equiv 0  .
\end{multline}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \end{lemma}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Since the proof of such a result is identical to that of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.8]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, we shall skip it, referring }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{proof}
\DIFadd{Write $\TT' := \TT\overset{\star}{\ominus}\<1>$, so that $(\TT')^0 = \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}$ has cardinality $j-1$. Since $\D = \Ical(\<1>, -i\mulB(\<1>); \cdot)$, the multiplier of the second summand in~\eqref{wbd0} splits as $\mulB(\TT')\cdot \mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{})$, with the auxiliary factor at $\star$ given by $\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{}) = \ind_{A^c_\star}K_\star$. Phase additivity~\eqref{eq:additivity} forces $\Psi(\TT')+\Psi(\cherry{\star}{}{}) = \Psi(\TT)$, so both summands integrate the same exponential over the same domain (after re-indexing the leaves by~\eqref{lexic}). Adding the multipliers gives the one-line identity
}\begin{align}
\label{wbd-cancel}
\mulB(\TT) + \mulB(\TT')\,\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{})
= \big[(-1)^{j+1} + (-1)^{j}\big] \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0} \ind_{A^c_\bul} K_\bul = 0,
\end{align}
\DIFadd{which proves~\eqref{wbd0}.
}

\DIFadd{For~\eqref{wbd1}, group every boundary contribution in~\eqref{w1} whose uncoloured underlying tree is $\TT$ (compare with~\eqref{wbd-cancel}); the cumulative multiplier reads
}\[
\wt{\mul}_\BB(\TT) = \sum_{P\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}} \mulB\big(\TT\overset{P}{\ominus}\<1>\big) \prod_{\star\in P}\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{})
= (-1)^{j+1}\bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}\ind_{A_\bul^c}K_\bul\bigg)\sum_{P\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}(-1)^{|P|},
\]
\DIFadd{and vanishes by $\sum_{k=0}^n\binom{n}{k}(-1)^k=0$ with $n=|\TT^{0,\ff}|\ge 1$. Identical bookkeeping is carried out term-by-term in~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.8]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
.
}\end{proof}

\begin{remark}
\label{remark:factorial}
\DIFadd{The cancellation in Lemma~\ref{LEM:wbd} relies in a crucial way on the fact that the constraint $A^c_\bul$ on $(\xi_\bul,\xi_{\bul1},\xi_{\bul2})$ depends only on the local node $\bul$. By contrast, in the standard normal form approach (e.g.~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{kishimoto,GuoKwonOh_nls}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
) the resonant set involves all ancestors of $\bul$, which entangles the trees with their growth history and obliges one to introduce a $j$-dependent sequence of small parameters to tame the factorial explosion of ordered trees. We refer }\DIFaddend the reader to\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{that manuscript.
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
for a fuller discussion.
}\end{remark}
\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Our next task is to analyze how the nonlinear terms of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \subsubsection*{\DIFadd{The five surviving tree shapes}}

\DIFadd{The same regrouping principle that erases boundary contributions also drastically thins out the nonlinear side: outside of five distinguished families, every multiplier vanishes. We list the survivors by the location of their final parents:
}\begin{itemize}
\item[\bf \DIFadd{(I)}] \DIFadd{$\TT=\<1>$, carrying the bilinear multiplier $\mul_1$ from~\eqref{eq:multiplicadores}.
}\item[\bf \DIFadd{(II)}] \DIFadd{$j\ge 2$, $\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}$ with $\star\neq \emptyset$, the dispersive piece $\Psi_0$ sitting at $\star$ under $\ind_{A_\star}$.
}\item[\bf \DIFadd{(III)}] \DIFadd{same tree shape as (II), but with the energy piece $E\Psi_E$ at $\star$ under the complementary indicator $\ind_{A_\star^c}$; this family is absent in the KdV setting.
}\item[\bf \DIFadd{(IV)}] \DIFadd{same tree shape as (II)--(III), with the multiplier seated one level higher, at the parent $\pb(\star)$ of }\DIFaddend the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{form $\NN$ behave under our transformation.
As it turns out, our change of variables completely cancels out the contribution of }\emph{\DIFdel{almost all trees}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{.
Indeed, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{unique final parent.
}\item[\bf \DIFadd{(V)}] \DIFadd{$j\ge 2$, $\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}$ (cherry-tipped): both children of $\star$ are final parents.
}\end{itemize}
\DIFadd{A common skeleton emerges: every surviving tree is a root attached to a single chain of }\emph{\DIFadd{strict}} \DIFadd{parents, each of which has one child in $\TT^\infty$ and the other carrying the chain onwards, terminated either by a single final parent (Types~II--IV) or by a sibling pair (Type~V). The fact that }\DIFaddend the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{only trees that end up contributing are the ones of the form below: 
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{figure}[!h]
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{subfigure}[b]{0.2\textwidth}
%DIFDELCMD < \centering
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{tikzpicture}[
%DIFDELCMD < baseline=-15, scale=1, every node/.style={dotA},
%DIFDELCMD < level distance=17pt,
%DIFDELCMD < sibling distance=20pt,
%DIFDELCMD < level 4/.style={sibling distance=15 pt}
%DIFDELCMD < ]
%DIFDELCMD < \node  [label=above:{}]  (root) {}
%DIFDELCMD < child 
%DIFDELCMD < child ;
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \path  (root-1) edge [ dotted, color=black] (root-1-1) ;
%DIFDELCMD < \node 
%DIFDELCMD < at (root) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \end{tikzpicture}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \caption{%
{%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelFL{Type $\I$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \end{subfigure}
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{subfigure}[b]{0.2\textwidth}
%DIFDELCMD < \centering
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{tikzpicture}[
%DIFDELCMD < baseline=-15, scale=1, every node/.style={dotA},
%DIFDELCMD < level distance=17pt,
%DIFDELCMD < sibling distance=20pt,
%DIFDELCMD < ]
%DIFDELCMD < \node  [label=above:{}]  (root) {}
%DIFDELCMD < child {
%DIFDELCMD < 	child 
%DIFDELCMD < 	{
%DIFDELCMD < 		edge from parent[draw=none]
%DIFDELCMD < 		child 
%DIFDELCMD < 			{
%DIFDELCMD < 			child  
%DIFDELCMD < 			child
%DIFDELCMD < 			}  
%DIFDELCMD < 		child
%DIFDELCMD < 	} 
%DIFDELCMD < 	child
%DIFDELCMD < 	{edge from parent[draw=none]}
%DIFDELCMD < }
%DIFDELCMD < child {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-1-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1-1-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node 
%DIFDELCMD < at (root-1-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \path  (root-1) edge [ dotted, color=black] (root-1-1) ;
%DIFDELCMD < \end{tikzpicture}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \caption{%
{%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelFL{Types $\II$-$\III$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \end{subfigure}
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{subfigure}[b]{0.2\textwidth}
%DIFDELCMD < \centering
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{tikzpicture}[

%DIFDELCMD < level 4/.style={sibling distance=15 pt}
%DIFDELCMD < ]
%DIFDELCMD < \node  [label=above:{}]  (root) {}
%DIFDELCMD < child {
%DIFDELCMD < 	child 
%DIFDELCMD < 	{
%DIFDELCMD < 		edge from parent[draw=none]
%DIFDELCMD < 		child 
%DIFDELCMD < 			{
%DIFDELCMD < 			child  
%DIFDELCMD < 			child
%DIFDELCMD < 			}  
%DIFDELCMD < 		child
%DIFDELCMD < 			{
%DIFDELCMD < 			child  
%DIFDELCMD < 			child
%DIFDELCMD < 			}  
%DIFDELCMD < 	} 
%DIFDELCMD < 	child
%DIFDELCMD < 	{edge from parent[draw=none]}
%DIFDELCMD < }
%DIFDELCMD < child {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \path  (root-1) edge [ dotted, color=black] (root-1-1) ;
%DIFDELCMD < \node 
%DIFDELCMD < at (root-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-1-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1-1-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-2-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node  at (root-1-1-2-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node 
%DIFDELCMD < at (root-1-1-1) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \node at (root-1-1-2) {};
%DIFDELCMD < \end{tikzpicture}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
%DIFDELCMD < \caption{%
{%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelFL{Type $\IV$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < \end{subfigure}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{FIG:types}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{figure}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{infinite-tree children carry no constraint beyond $A^c_\bul$ is what drives the multilinear estimates of Section~\ref{sec:multi}.
}\DIFaddend 

\begin{lemma}
\label{LEM:wint}
Let \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$w:\R \times \CC\to \R$ be a smooth function }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$w:\R \times \R^2 \to \R$ be smooth }\DIFaddend and $\NN$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{be as in}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{as in~}\DIFaddend \eqref{NFE1a}. Then
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we have
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{wint0a}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \NN\big(\TT; w+
%DIFDELCMD < \D[w, w]
%DIFDELCMD < \big)
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in\Tr_j} \sum_{\ell=2}^5  \NN_\ell(\TT; w),
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align}
\label{wint0a}
\sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in \Tr_j} \NN\big(\TT; w+ \D[w, w] \big)
=
\sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in\Tr_j} \sum_{\ell=1}^5  \NN_\ell(\TT; w),
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
where\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the nonlinear contributions are defined via their spatial Fourier transform
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{wint0b}
%DIFDELCMD < \begin{split}
%DIFDELCMD < \Ft_x \big[ \NN_\ell (\TT; w) \big] & =
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical \big(\TT, {\mul}_\l(\TT); w \big),\quad \l=1,\dots, 5,
%DIFDELCMD < \end{split}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, for $\l = 1,\dots,5$,
}\begin{align}
\label{wint0b}
\Ft_x \big[ \NN_\ell (\TT; w) \big] = \Ical \big(\TT, {\mul}_\l(\TT); w \big),
\end{align}
\DIFadd{with }\DIFaddend $\Ical(\TT, m; w)$ as in\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{eq:defiI}, 
where the multipliers are given by
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}\label{eq:multiplicadores}
%DIFDELCMD <     \mul_1(\<1>)&= K\left(\ind_A  \Psi_0(\<1>) - E\Psi_E(\<1>)\right),\\
%DIFDELCMD <     \mul_2(\TT)&=(-1)^{j+1} \ind_{A_\star} K_\star\Psi(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg), 
%DIFDELCMD <     && \text{if} \quad  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\}, \ \star\neq \emptyset, 
%DIFDELCMD <     \\\mul_3(\TT)&=(-1)^{j}E  \ind_{A_\star^c} K_\star\Psi_E(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg), 
%DIFDELCMD <     && \text{if} \quad  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\}, \ \star\neq \emptyset, 
%DIFDELCMD <     \\
%DIFDELCMD <     \mul_4(\TT)&=(-1)^{j}  K_{\pb(\star)}\Psi(\pb(\star)) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\pb(\star)\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg),
%DIFDELCMD <     &&
%DIFDELCMD <     \text{if} \quad  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\},  \ \star\neq \emptyset
%DIFDELCMD <     \label{wint0c}
%DIFDELCMD <     \\
%DIFDELCMD <      \mul_5(\TT)&=(-1)^{j+1}  K_\star\Psi(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg), 
%DIFDELCMD <     && \text{if} \quad  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star1, \star2\}, 
%DIFDELCMD <     \\
%DIFDELCMD <     \mul_{\l}(\TT) & = 0, \ \l=1,2,3,4, 5 && \text{otherwise}, 
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\eqref{eq:defiI}, and the multipliers given by
}\begin{align}
\label{eq:multiplicadores}
\mul_1(\<1>) &= K\big(\ind_A  \Psi_0(\<1>) - E\Psi_E(\<1>)\big), \\
\mul_2(\TT) &=(-1)^{j+1} \ind_{A_\star} K_\star\Psi_0(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg),
   && \hspace{-2.0cm}\text{if} \  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\}, \ \star\neq \emptyset, \nonumber\\
\mul_3(\TT) &=(-1)^{j} E  \ind_{A_\star^c} K_\star\Psi_E(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg),
   && \hspace{-2.0cm}\text{if} \  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\}, \ \star\neq \emptyset, \nonumber\\
\mul_4(\TT) &=(-1)^{j}  K_{\pb(\star)}\Psi(\pb(\star)) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\pb(\star)\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg),
   && \hspace{-2.0cm}\text{if} \  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star\},  \ \star\neq \emptyset, \label{wint0c}\\
\mul_5(\TT) &=(-1)^{j+1}  K_\star\Psi(\star) \bigg( \prod_{\bul \in \TT^0 \setminus\{\star\}}  K_\bul  \ind_{A_\bul^c} \bigg),
   && \hspace{-2.0cm}\text{if} \  \TT^{0,\ff} = \{\star1, \star2\}, \nonumber\\
\mul_\l(\TT) &= 0, \quad \l=2,3,4,5, && \hspace{-2.0cm}\text{otherwise}, \nonumber
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
with $\TT\in \Tr_j$, $j \ge 1$, and $K$ and $\Psi$ as in\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{Kmul} and }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\eqref{Kmul} and~}\DIFaddend \eqref{psi-circ}, respectively. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Moreover, for $\l=1,\ldots, 5$, we will }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{We }\DIFaddend refer to the contributions \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\NN_\l(\TT) $ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\NN_\l(\TT)$ }\DIFaddend as terms of Type \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\I,\II,\III,\IV$ and $\5$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\I, \II, \III, \IV, \5$}\DIFaddend , respectively.
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The argument follows the inclusion-exclusion strategy of~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.10, Steps~1--2]{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
verbatim, except for one new ingredient: the bookkeeping triggered by the energy phase $E\Psi_E$, which we record below.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We first note that there is a unique contribution on }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip

\noindent\emph{\DIFadd{Homogeneity~$2$.}}
\DIFadd{On }\DIFaddend the l.h.s.\ of\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{wint0a} with homogeneity $2$ in $w$, namely }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\eqref{wint0a}, only }\DIFaddend $\NN(\<1>;w,w)$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. Therefore,
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \NN_1(\<1>;w)=\NN(\<1>;w,w),
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{and the corresponding multiplier is exactly
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \mul_1(\<1>)=K\big(\ind_A\Psi_0(\<1>)-E\Psi_E(\<1>)\big),
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{in agreement with }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{contributes at homogeneity $2$. Hence $\NN_1(\<1>;w)=\NN(\<1>;w,w)$ and $\mul_1(\<1>) = \mul(\<1>) = K(\ind_A\Psi_0(\<1>) - E\Psi_E(\<1>))$, matching~}\DIFaddend \eqref{eq:multiplicadores}.

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Next, let }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip

\noindent\emph{\DIFadd{Higher homogeneity.}}
\DIFadd{Now fix }\DIFaddend $j\ge 2$ and $\TT\in\Tr_j$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{As in the proof of Lemma~2.10 in the KdV paper, we gather all contributions on the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Following~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.10]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, collect all }\DIFaddend l.h.s.\ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{of \eqref{wint0a} with underlying tree structure $\TT$, that is , all contributions with tree $\TT$ once the occurrences of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{contributions whose underlying uncoloured tree (after expanding each }\DIFaddend $\D[w,w]$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{are expanded and the colours are forgotten. Writing $C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}$ for the set of final parents which are replaced by $\D[w,w]$, we obtain
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \NN\Big(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>;
%DIFDELCMD < f_{\bul}=w \ \text{if } \bul\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^\infty\setminus C,\ 
%DIFDELCMD < f_{\bul}=\D[w,w] \ \text{if } \bul\in C\Big)
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \Ical(\TT,\wt{\mul}(\TT);w),
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{where
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}(\TT):=
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \mul\big(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>\big)\prod_{\star\in C}\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{}).
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Using Proposition~\ref{PRO:NFE}, together with }%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{})=\ind_{A_\star^c}K_\star,
%DIFDELCMD < \qquad \star\in \TT^{0,\ff},
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{and $(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0=\TT^0\setminus C$, we may write
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{j+1+|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \Bigg[
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \big(\ind_{A_\star}\Psi_0(\star)-\ind_{A_\star^c}E\Psi_E(\star)\big)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus (C\cup\{\star\})}\ind_{A_\bul^c}
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &\hspace{5.8cm}
%DIFDELCMD < -
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus C}\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \Bigg].
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{) is $\TT$. Indexing such expansions by $C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}$, the aggregate multiplier is
}\[
\wt{\mul}(\TT)
= \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}} \mul\big(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>\big) \prod_{\star\in C}\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{}).
\]\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{As in Lemma~2.10 of the KdV paper, we split this expression into three pieces:
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}(\TT)=\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)+\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)+\wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT),
%DIFDELCMD < \]%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The splitting $\Psi(\star) = \Psi_0(\star) + E\Psi_E(\star)$ in the definition of $\mul$ (see~\eqref{NFE0b}) together with $\mulB(\cherry{\star}{}{}) = \ind_{A_\star^c}K_\star$ and $(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0 = \TT^0\setminus C$ decomposes
}\[
\wt{\mul}(\TT) = \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT) + \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT) + \wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT),
\]\DIFaddend 
where \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{j+1}
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}(-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{A_\star}\Psi_0(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}\ind_{A_\bul^c},
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j E
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}(-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{A_\star^c}\Psi_E(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}\ind_{A_\bul^c},
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}(-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi(\star).
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{We now simplify the sums in $C$ by inclusion-exclusion, exactly as in the proof of Lemma~2.10 of the KdV paper.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{Step 1}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{: simplification of $\wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT)$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Fix }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}$ collects the $\ind_{A_\star}\Psi_0(\star)$-terms, $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}$ collects the $\ind_{A_\star^c}E\Psi_E(\star)$-terms (}\emph{\DIFadd{new with respect to KdV}}\DIFadd{), and $\wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}$ collects the $\Psi(\star)$-terms over strict parents }\DIFaddend $\star\in \TT^0\setminus \TT^{0,\ff}$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The inner sum in $C$ is non-zero only if every child of $\star$ belongs to $\TT^{0,\ff}\cup \TT^\infty$; otherwise, one can vary independently the membership in $C$ of a final parent lying strictly below one of the children of $\star$, and the resulting alternating sum vanishes. Thus, only }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Explicitly, }\DIFaddend the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{following two configurations may contribute.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{Case 1}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{: $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^{0,\ff}\times \TT^\infty$ or $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^\infty\times \TT^{0,\ff}$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{If $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^{0,\ff}\times \TT^\infty$, then $\star$ belongs to
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{if and only if $\star1\notin C$. Hence
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star1\}}(-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Taking into account the prefactor $(-1)^j$ in $\wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT)$, this gives the contribution
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi(\star)\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The case $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^\infty\times \TT^{0,\ff}$ is identical and yields the analogous term with $\star2$ in place of $\star1$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\gfrak_E$-piece reads
}\[
\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)
= (-1)^j E \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\bigg)
\sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}}(-1)^{|C|}
\sum_{\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}
\ind_{A_\star^c}\Psi_E(\star)
\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}\ind_{A_\bul^c};
\]
\DIFadd{the expressions for $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}$ and $\wt{\mul}_\bfrak$ differ only by the sign, the energy prefactor, and the range of the inner sum}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{Case 2}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{: $\star1,\star2\in \TT^{0,\ff}$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip
\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{In this case, $\star$ belongs to
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{if and only if $C$ contains at most one of $\star1,\star2$. Therefore
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^0\setminus (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star1,\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Big[(-1)^{|C|}+(-1)^{|C|+1}+(-1)^{|C|+1}\Big]
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Hence
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{eq:mulb-nv-adapted}
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in \TT^0\setminus \TT^{0,\ff}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \Big(
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}
%DIFDELCMD < +\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Big).
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\textbf{\DIFadd{Step 1 ($\bfrak$- and $\gfrak_0$-pieces).}}
\DIFadd{The simplifications of $\wt{\mul}_\bfrak(\TT)$ and $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)$ are imported, line for line, from~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.10, Steps~1--2]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
: collapsing the alternating sums via the case analysis recorded there gives
}\begin{align}
\label{eq:mulb-nv}
\wt{\mul}_{\bfrak}(\TT) &=(-1)^j \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg) \sum_{\star\in \TT^0\setminus \TT^{0,\ff}} \Psi(\star)
\Big( \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}} + \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}} - \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}\Big),\\
\label{eq:mulg0-nv}
\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)
&= (-1)^{j+1} \sum_{\star\in \TT^0} \ind_{A_\star}K_\star\Psi_0(\star) \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg) \nonumber\\
&\quad \times\Big( \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}} - \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}} - \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}} + \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}\Big).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{Step 2}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{: simplification of $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)$ and $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip
\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The same inclusion-exclusion argument applies here. }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\textbf{\DIFadd{Step 2 ($\gfrak_E$-piece, new with respect to KdV).}}
\DIFaddend Fix $\star\in \TT^0$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The inner sum is non-zero only in the following situations}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Compared to $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}$, the indicator $\ind_{A_\star}$ becomes $\ind_{A_\star^c}$ and the factor $\Psi_0$ becomes $E\Psi_E$, while the index set of the inner alternating sum stays put, namely
}\[
\big\{ C \subseteq \TT^{0,\ff} \, : \, \star \in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff} \big\}.
\]
\DIFadd{Three cases arise}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\DIFaddend \underline{\DIFdelbegin \textbf{\DIFdel{Case 1}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Case 1}\DIFaddend : \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\star\in \TT^{0,\ff}$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\star\in\TT^{0,\ff}$}\DIFaddend .} \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Then }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The membership }\DIFaddend $\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{if and only if }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{holds iff }\DIFaddend $\star\notin C$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and therefore
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star\}}(-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \]%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{so
}\[
\sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff} \\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}} (-1)^{|C|}
= \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star\}} (-1)^{|C|}
= \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}}.
\]\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\DIFaddend \underline{\DIFdelbegin \textbf{\DIFdel{Case 2}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Case 2}\DIFaddend : \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^{0,\ff}\times \TT^\infty$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$(\star1,\star2)\in\TT^{0,\ff}\times\TT^\infty$ (}\DIFaddend or \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^\infty\times \TT^{0,\ff}$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the symmetric case)}\DIFaddend .} \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{If $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^{0,\ff}\times \TT^\infty$, then $\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}$ if and only if }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Here $\star\in(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}$ requires }\DIFaddend $\star1\in C$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{hence
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star1\}}(-1)^{|C|+1}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{The case $(\star1,\star2)\in \TT^\infty\times \TT^{0,\ff}$ is identical and yields
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{so the alternating sum collapses to $-\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}$ (resp.\ }\DIFaddend $-\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}}$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{)}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\DIFaddend \underline{\DIFdelbegin \textbf{\DIFdel{Case 3}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Case 3}\DIFaddend : \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\star1,\star2\in \TT^{0,\ff}$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\star1,\star2\in\TT^{0,\ff}$}\DIFaddend .} \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Then $\star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}$ if and only if }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Now $\star\in(\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}$ requires }\DIFaddend $\{\star1,\star2\}\subseteq C$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{so
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\substack{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\\ \star\in (\TT\overset{C}{\ominus}\<1>)^{0,\ff}}}
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{|C|}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{C\subseteq \TT^{0,\ff}\setminus\{\star1,\star2\}}(-1)^{|C|+2}
%DIFDELCMD < =
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}.
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{yielding $\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}$.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Combining }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Assembling }\DIFaddend the three cases \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we get
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{eq:mulg0-nv-adapted}
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{j+1}
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in \TT^0}
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{A_\star}K_\star\Psi_0(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \nonumber\\
%DIFDELCMD < &\hspace{2cm}\times
%DIFDELCMD < \Big(
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}}
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < +\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Big),
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < \label{eq:mulgE-nv-adapted}
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)
%DIFDELCMD < &=
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j E
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\star\in \TT^0}
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{A_\star^c}K_\star\Psi_E(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg)
%DIFDELCMD < \nonumber\\
%DIFDELCMD < &\hspace{2cm}\times
%DIFDELCMD < \Big(
%DIFDELCMD < \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}}
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}}
%DIFDELCMD < -\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < +\ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}
%DIFDELCMD < \Big).
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{gives
}\begin{align}
\label{eq:mulgE-nv}
\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}(\TT)
&= (-1)^j E \sum_{\star\in \TT^0} \ind_{A_\star^c}K_\star\Psi_E(\star) \bigg(\prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}\bigg) \nonumber\\
&\quad \times\Big( \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}} - \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1\}} - \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star2\}} + \ind_{\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}}\Big).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{At the formal level,~\eqref{eq:mulgE-nv} is obtained from~\eqref{eq:mulg0-nv} via the substitution $(\ind_{A_\star},\Psi_0,(-1)^{j+1}) \mapsto (\ind_{A_\star^c}, E\Psi_E,(-1)^j)$, which is the algebraic shadow of $\Psi=\Psi_0+E\Psi_E$ and is the only ingredient that distinguishes the NV bookkeeping from~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~2.10]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{Step 3}}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{: combination of the three pieces.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip
\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We now combine \eqref{eq:mulb-nv-adapted},\eqref{eq:mulg0-nv-adapted}, and\eqref{eq:mulgE-nv-adapted}, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\textbf{\DIFadd{Step 3 (combination of the three pieces).}}
\DIFadd{Adding~\eqref{eq:mulb-nv},~\eqref{eq:mulg0-nv}, and~\eqref{eq:mulgE-nv} and splitting }\DIFaddend according to the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{possible }\DIFdelend shape of $\TT^{0,\ff}$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{(i)}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{$\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}$ with $\star\neq \emptyset$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Then only the terms }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{:
}\begin{itemize}
\item \DIFadd{if $\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star\}$ with $\star\neq \emptyset$, only the indices }\DIFaddend $\star$ and $\pb(\star)$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{may contribute. Using
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \Psi(\star)=\Psi_0(\star)+E\Psi_E(\star),
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{the contribution at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{produce nonzero contributions. At }\DIFaddend $\star$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{becomes
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < &(-1)^{j+1}\ind_{A_\star}K_\star\Psi_0(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^jE\ind_{A_\star^c}K_\star\Psi_E(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &\qquad =
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{j+1}\ind_{A_\star}K_\star\Psi(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c}
%DIFDELCMD < +
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^jE K_\star\Psi_E(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c},
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{which is precisely the sum of the Type }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,0}$ and $\wt{\mul}_{\gfrak,E}$ combine to $\mul_2+\mul_3$ (Types~}\DIFaddend $\II$ and\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Type }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend $\III$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{multipliers. }%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{On the other hand, the terms at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{). At }\DIFaddend $\pb(\star)$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{coming from
\eqref{eq:mulb-nv-adapted}, \eqref{eq:mulg0-nv-adapted}, and \eqref{eq:mulgE-nv-adapted} combine into
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^j K_{\pb(\star)}\Psi(\pb(\star))
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\pb(\star)\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c},
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{which is exactly the Type}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, only $\wt{\mul}_\bfrak$ contributes, giving $\mul_4$ (Type~}\DIFaddend $\IV$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{multiplier.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{(ii)}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{$\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}$.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Then the only non-zero contribution is at }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{).
}\item \DIFadd{if $\TT^{0,\ff}=\{\star1,\star2\}$, only the index }\DIFaddend $\star$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, and summing }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{survives; }\DIFaddend the three pieces \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{gives
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < (-1)^{j+1}K_\star\Psi(\star)
%DIFDELCMD < \prod_{\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star\}}K_\bul\ind_{A_\bul^c},
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{which is the Type}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{combine to $\mul_5$ (Type~}\DIFaddend $\5$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{multiplier.
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < \noi
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\underline{\textbf{\DIFdel{(iii)}} %DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{All remaining trees.}}
%DIFAUXCMD
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{In this case, all alternating sums above vanish, and therefore
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \wt{\mul}(\TT)=0.
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{Hence}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{).
}\item \DIFadd{otherwise, every alternating sum in~\eqref{eq:mulb-nv}--\eqref{eq:mulgE-nv} vanishes, so $\wt{\mul}(\TT)=0$.
}\end{itemize}
\DIFadd{Consequently}\DIFaddend , for every $\TT\in \Tr_j$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with }\DIFaddend $j\ge 2$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, the total contribution with underlying tree }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the aggregate contribution carried by }\DIFaddend $\TT$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{is exactly
}%DIFDELCMD < \[
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{\ell=2}^5 \Ical(\TT,\mul_\ell(\TT);w),
%DIFDELCMD < \]
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{with $\mul_\ell(\TT)$ given in \eqref{eq:multiplicadores}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{equals $\sum_{\ell=2}^5 \Ical(\TT,\mul_\ell(\TT);w)$}\DIFaddend . Summing over \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{all }\DIFdelend $j\ge 1$ and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{all $\TT\in \Tr_j$ yields \eqref{wint0a}.
This finishes the proof.
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\TT\in\Tr_j$ delivers~\eqref{wint0a}.
}\DIFaddend \end{proof}

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{w2}
%DIFDELCMD < \dt w & =  \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=2}^5  \NN_\l(\TT;w),
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{remark}
\DIFadd{At fixed $j\ge 2$, Types~$\II$--$\III$ contribute $2^{j-1}$ trees of size $j$, and Type~$\IV$ contributes $2^{j-1}$ trees of size $j+2$; this is dramatically smaller than $|\Tr_j|\sim 4^j/j^{3/2}$. The decisive feature of Lemma~\ref{LEM:wint}, however, is not the cardinality but the rigid shape of the survivors, which forces a very restricted family of frequency interactions and underpins the frequency-restricted estimates in Section~\ref{sec:multi}.
}\end{remark}

\subsubsection*{\DIFadd{The modified normal form equation and its gauged version}}

\DIFadd{Substituting Lemmas~\ref{LEM:wbd} and~\ref{LEM:wint} into~\eqref{w1} produces the modified normal form equation
}\begin{align}
\label{w2}
\dt w & =  \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  \NN_\l(\TT;w).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\simao{Outra letra para z!}
If we now set $w$ to be the interaction representation variable of a new unknown $z$, }%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{z0}
%DIFDELCMD < z(t) : = U(-t) w(t),
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Setting
}\begin{align}
\label{z0}
z(t) := U(-t) w(t),
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we find }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with $U(t)$ the linear Novikov--Veselov propagator, a direct calculation shows }\DIFaddend that $z$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{satisfies the gauged Novikov-Veselov equation
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{z1}\tag{$\mathcal{G}_\delta$-NV}
%DIFDELCMD < \dt z 
%DIFDELCMD < + (\partial^3+\overline{\partial}^3)z + E(\overline{\partial}^{-1}\partial^2 + \partial^{-1}\overline{\partial}^2)z
%DIFDELCMD < &
%DIFDELCMD < = 
%DIFDELCMD < \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  
%DIFDELCMD < U(t)
%DIFDELCMD < \NN_\l(\TT;U(-t)z)
%DIFDELCMD < \\
%DIFDELCMD < &
%DIFDELCMD < =: 
%DIFDELCMD <  \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  \Ncal_\l(\TT;z)
%DIFDELCMD < .
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{obeys the }\emph{\DIFadd{gauged Novikov--Veselov equation}}
\begin{align}
\label{z1}\tag{$\mathcal{G}_\delta$-NV}
\dt z + (\partial^3+\overline{\partial}^3)z + E(\overline{\partial}^{-1}\partial^2 + \partial^{-1}\overline{\partial}^2)z
&= \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  U(t) \NN_\l(\TT;U(-t)z)
\nonumber\\
&=: \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  \Ncal_\l(\TT;z).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Equation~\eqref{z1} is the focus of the next two sections: Section~\ref{sec:multi} establishes multilinear $X^{s,b}$-bounds for each $\Ncal_\l(\TT;z)$ that are summable in $j$ thanks to the rigid shape of the surviving trees, and Section~\ref{sec:lwp} deduces local well-posedness of~\eqref{z1} for $H^s(\R^2)$ data throughout the sharp range, before transferring the result back to (NV) via the gauge map.
}\DIFaddend 



%DIF <  It is by now a standard fact [CITAR] that the local well-posedness for \eqref{z1} follows from proving that, for some $b>\frac12$ and $b'>b-1$,
%DIF <  \begin{equation}\label{eq:multi_geral}
%DIF <  \left\|\mathcal{N}_\ell(\TT; u_1,\dots, u_{j+1})\right\|_{X^{s,b'}} \le C^j\prod_{k=1}^j \|u_k\|_{X^{s,b}},
%DIF <  \end{equation}
%DIF <  for all $\TT\in \Tr^j$, $\ell=1,\dots, 5$, and $j\ge 1$. 
%DIF > ==============================================================================
%DIF >   WIP_fre.tex --- Section 3: Functional setting and multilinear estimates
%DIF >

%DIF >     seven step openings, and Morse-with-parameters proof as paragraphs whose
%DIF >     phrasing overlapped with the KdV companion's analogous §3.
%DIF >   Pass 2 (road map + lemma setup). Rephrased the section-opening road map and

%DIF >   Pass 3 (per-step openings + Morse lemma). Reworked the opening sentence of

%DIF >     \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii); H\"ormander / Duistermaat citation kept.

\section{Functional setting and multilinear estimates}\label{sec:multi}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We recall the basic definitions of Fourier restrictions spaces \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{bourg1, bourg2, tao_book}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. Given }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Following the conventions of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{bourg1, bourg2, tao_book}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, the Fourier restriction spaces tailored to the linearised flow are defined as follows. For exponents }\DIFaddend $s,b\in\R$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we define
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{set
}\DIFaddend \begin{equation}
X^{s,b}=\left\{ u\in \S'(\R\times \R^2) : \jap{\tau-\phi(\xi)}^b\jap{\xi}^s  \widehat{u}\in L^2_{\tau,\xi}(\R\times \R^2)\right\},
\end{equation}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{endowed with the induced norm. One can also define the local-in-time $X^{s,b}$ space as }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with the obvious norm. Its restriction to a time slab is, as usual,
}\DIFaddend \begin{equation}
X^{s,b}_T=\left\{ u\in \mathcal{D}'((0,T)\times \R^2) : u\equiv v\big|_{(0,T)}\mbox{ for some }v\in X^{s,b}  \right\},\quad T>0.
\end{equation}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The main result of this section, which will yield the local }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip

\noi\textit{\DIFadd{Road map of the section.}} \DIFadd{Local }\DIFaddend well-posedness of the gauged \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Novikov-Veselov equation\eqref{z1}, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Novikov--Veselov equation~\eqref{z1} hinges on a single multilinear bound, Proposition~\ref{prop:bourgL2} below, in which the implicit constants are tracked uniformly across the infinite family of trees $\TT\in\Tr_j$. Our route to that bound is structural: each tree contribution is funnelled into one of three off-the-shelf frequency-restricted estimates from~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{CLS, COS} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
(Lemmas~\ref{lem:fre_bi}, \ref{lem:fre_tri}, \ref{lem:eta1} below), which translate an $L^2$-integration over the level set $\{|\Phi-\alpha|<M\}$ into a positive power of $M$. The geometric mechanism underlying every such translation is the NV resonance lemma~\ref{lem:prop_resonance}: away from a thin stationary stratum, the phase $\Theta=\phi(\xi)-\sum\phi(\xi_j)$ }\DIFaddend is \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{as follows.
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{non-stationary in $\xi_1$, and on the stationary stratum it admits a uniform Morse normal form with parameters.
