The proof of Proposition~\ref{prop:bourgL2} is then organised into seven steps, indexed by the tree type $\ell\in\{1,\dots,5\}$ and by whether the length $j$ is below or above the threshold dictated by the cluster of the focal node $\star$.
}

\DIFaddend \begin{proposition}\label{prop:bourgL2}
Let $s>-1$, $E\in\CC$ with $|E|<1$, $0<\delta\ll 1$ and $T>0$. Given $j \in\N$, $\TT \in \Tr_j$, and $\Ncal_\l(\TT)$, $\l=1,\dots,5$, there exists $b>\frac{1}{2}$ such that
	\begin{align}\label{eq:bourg_bi_l2}
		\left\|\int_0^t U(t-t') \Ncal_\l(\TT; z_1,\dots, z_{j+1})(t') dt'  \right\|_{X^{s,b}_T}  \le T^{0+} C^j\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}\prod_{k=1}^{j+1}\|z_k\|_{X^{s,b}_T}
	\end{align}
    for some constant $C>0$ independent of $j$ and $\TT$.
\end{proposition}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{In order to prove Proposition\ref{prop:bourgL2}, we resort }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{remark}\label{rmk:exponent_optimal}
\DIFadd{For $s>-1$ one has $2s+2>0$, and the seven steps below actually produce the sharper bounds $\delta^{-1}$ for $j=1$, $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-2)}$ in Step~2, $1$ for $j=2,3$ in Steps~3 and~6, and $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$ for $j\ge 3$ in Steps~4 and~7. Each of these is dominated by $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}$, the only step requiring the extra $\delta^{-1}$ factor being Step~1 (Type~I). The uniform exponent in \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2} is convenient for the geometric-series argument in Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv}, whose summability is guaranteed by~\eqref{eq:escolhadelta}.
}\end{remark}

\DIFadd{The route from Proposition~\ref{prop:bourgL2} }\DIFaddend to frequency-restricted estimates \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{COS}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
. For the sake of completeness, we include below the necessary lemmas for quadratic and higher-order terms, respectively}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is by now standard; for the convenience of the reader we collect below the precise statements that we shall plug into our case analysis. The bilinear and higher-multilinear versions appear separately, since the second admits a non-trivial splitting of the multiplier}\DIFaddend .

\begin{lemma}[{\cite[Lemma 3.1]{CLS}}]\label{lem:fre_bi}
Let $s\in\R$.
Suppose that, for all $\al\in \R$ and $M>1$, there exists $0<\beta<1$, such that one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item[(i)] for all distinct $ k, \l\in\{\emptyset,1,2\}$\footnote{The \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{empty set }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{empty-set }\DIFaddend symbol $\emptyset$ here corresponds to the frequency component $\xi$, without index.}
    and $1<M\lesssim |\alpha|$,
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:frequad}
        \sup_{\xi_k}\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2}
        \frac{|m_1(\<1>)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{1}}^{2s}\jap{\xi_{2}}^{2s}}\mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{\l} \lesssim \jap{\alpha}^\beta M^\beta;
    \end{equation}

    %DIF <  \item[(ii)]
    %DIF <  there exist distinct $k, \l\in\{1,2\}$ such that
    %DIF <  \begin{equation}\label{eq:frequad2}
    %DIF <      \sup_{\xi_k}\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2}
    %DIF <      \frac{|m_1(\<1>)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{1}}^{2s}\jap{\xi_{2}}^{2s}}\mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{\l}  \lesssim \jap{\alpha} M^\beta;
    %DIF <  \end{equation}
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD <     
%DIFDELCMD <     %%%
\DIFdelend \item[(ii)] or we have that
    \DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:frequad3}
%DIFDELCMD <         \sup_{\xi}\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2}\frac{|m_1(\<1>)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{1}}^{2s}\jap{\xi_{2}}^{2s}}\mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{1}  \lesssim \jap{\alpha}^\beta M;
%DIFDELCMD <     \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:frequad3}
        \sup_{\xi}\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2}\frac{|m_1(\<1>)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{1}}^{2s}\jap{\xi_{2}}^{2s}}\mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{1}  \lesssim \jap{\alpha}^\beta M.
    \end{equation}\DIFaddend 
\end{enumerate}
Then there exists $b>\frac{1}{2}$ such that \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2} holds for $\ell=1$ and $\TT=\<1>$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[{\cite[Lemma 2]{COS}}]\label{lem:fre_tri}
Let $s\in\R$, $j\ge 1$, $\ell=2,\dots,5$, and $\TT\in \Tr^j$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Suppose that there exists }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Let }\DIFaddend $B\subset \{\emptyset, 1, \ldots, j+1\}$ be a proper non-empty subset, and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\M_1 , \M_2: \CC^{j} \to \R^+$ be multipliers satisfying
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD <     \frac{|m_\ell(\TT)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\prod_{k=1}^j\jap{\xi_{k}}^{2s}}
%DIFDELCMD <     \les 
%DIFDELCMD <     \M_1(\vec\xi) \M_2(\vec\xi),
%DIFDELCMD <     \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{suppose that $\M_1, \M_2:\CC^{j} \to \R^+$ are multipliers satisfying
}\begin{align}
\frac{|m_\ell(\TT)|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\prod_{k=1}^j\jap{\xi_{k}}^{2s}}
\les
\M_1(\vec\xi)\,\M_2(\vec\xi),
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
where $\vec\xi=(\xi_1, \ldots, \xi_{j+1})$.
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Then, if }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{If }\DIFaddend there exists $0<\be<1$ such that
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{L2hypo}
%DIFDELCMD <     \sup_{\xi_{k\in B}} \int_{\Gamma(\TT)} \mathcal{M}_1 (\vec\xi) \mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{j\notin B} + \sup_{\xi_{j\notin B}} \int_{\Gamma(\TT)} \mathcal{M}_2 (\vec\xi) \mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{j\in B} \lesssim C^j M^\beta, 
%DIFDELCMD <     \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{L2hypo}
\sup_{\xi_{k\in B}} \int_{\Gamma(\TT)} \mathcal{M}_1 (\vec\xi)\, \mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{j\notin B}
+ \sup_{\xi_{j\notin B}} \int_{\Gamma(\TT)} \mathcal{M}_2 (\vec\xi)\, \mathbbm{1}_{|\Phi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{j\in B}
\lesssim C^j M^\beta,
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
for all $M\ge 1$ and $\al\in\R$,
then there exists $b>\frac{1}{2}$, depending only on $\be$, such that \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2} holds.
\end{lemma}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The restriction $\beta<1$ in Lemmas \ref{lem:fre_bi} and \ref{lem:fre_tri} can be improved to $\beta=1$ at the expense of slightly increasing the weight of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin 

\DIFadd{The endpoint $\beta=1$ in the hypotheses of Lemmas~\ref{lem:fre_bi} and~\ref{lem:fre_tri} is not literally allowed, but it can be reached at the price of a small weight on }\DIFaddend the largest frequency\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, as the next useful lemma shows}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{. The following technical statement formalises this trade-off and will be invoked tacitly in every step of the proof}\DIFaddend .

\begin{lemma}[{\cite[Lemma 3.3]{CLS}}]\label{lem:eta1}
    Let $K:\R^n\times \R^m\times \R\to \R^+$ be a positive measurable function such that, for some $N\in \mathbb{N}$,
    $$
    |K(x,y,M)|\lesssim \max\{1,|x|,|y|\}^N,\quad \forall x\in\R^n,\ y\in \R^m, \ M\in \R.
    $$
    Suppose that
    $$
    \sup_y \int K(x,y,M)\max\{1,|x|,|y|\}^{0+} dx \lesssim M,\quad \mbox{for all }M>1.
    $$
    Then, there exists $0<\beta<1$ such that
    $$
    \sup_y \int K(x,y,M) dx \lesssim M^{\beta},\quad \mbox{for all } M>1.
    $$
\end{lemma}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{The next ingredient concerns the geometry }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{We turn next to the geometric heart of the proof: the behaviour }\DIFaddend of the resonance \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{functions }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{function }\DIFaddend $\Psi(\TT)$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and is the crux of the multilinear estimates \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2}. These properties can also be linked with the optimal decay in the Strichartz estimates associated with the Novikov-Veselov equation }%DIFDELCMD < [%%%
\DIFdel{CITE}%DIFDELCMD < ]%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{on the support of the tree integral. The dichotomy below -- non-stationary in $\xi_1$ off a thin set, Morse with parameters on it -- is precisely the analytic content driving the optimal Strichartz estimates obtained in~\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{kazeykinamunoz1, kazeykinamunoz2} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
for the linear Novikov--Veselov propagator, and reflects the convexity properties of $\phi(\xi)=\Re\xi^3$}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\simao{Expandir isto num comentário.}
}%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \begin{lemma}\label{lem:prop_resonance}
Fix $|E|<1$ and $k\ge 2$. Consider the mapping $\Theta:\CC^{k}\to \R$
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \Theta(\xi_1,\dots, \xi_{k})= \phi(\xi)-\sum_{j=1}^k \phi(\xi_j),\quad \xi=\sum_{j=1}^{k} \xi_j
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin $$
\Theta(\xi_1,\dots, \xi_{k})= \phi(\xi)-\sum_{j=1}^k \phi(\xi_j),\quad \xi=\sum_{j=1}^{k} \xi_j.
$$\DIFaddend 

\noi{\rm (i)} Over the region
\begin{equation}
V=\left\{\vec{\xi}\in \CC^{k} :\  \frac{1}{\delta}<|\xi_1|,\  |\xi_1\pm\xi|>\delta\max\{|\xi_1|, |\xi|\}\right\},
\end{equation}
we have
$$
|\nabla_{\xi_1}\Theta|\ge 2\delta^2\max\{|\xi_1|^2, |\xi|^2\}.
$$

\noi{\rm (ii)} Suppose that
$$
|\xi_1|\ge |\xi_2| \ge |\xi|\ge |\xi_3|\ge \dots \ge |\xi_k|.
$$
There exist $\delta, \delta'>0$, independent of $k$, and a change of coordinates
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \varphi:U=\{\vec{\xi}\in \CC^{k} :\  \frac{1}{\delta}<|\xi_1|,\  |\xi_1+\xi|<\delta|\xi_1|\} \mapsto B_{\delta'}(0)\times \CC^{k-1}\\ \vec{\xi} \to (q_1, \xi_2, \dots, \xi_k)
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align*}
\varphi:U=\{\vec{\xi}\in \CC^{k} :\  \tfrac{1}{\delta}<|\xi_1|,\  |\xi_1+\xi|<\delta|\xi_1|\} \mapsto B_{\delta'}(0)\times \CC^{k-1}\\ \vec{\xi}\mapsto (q_1, \xi_2, \dots, \xi_k)
\end{align*}\DIFaddend 
satisfying
\begin{equation}\label{eq:nondeg}
|\det D_{\xi_1}\varphi| \sim |\xi_2|^{-2}
\end{equation}
and
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \Theta(\vec{\xi})=|\xi_2|^3\Re q_1^2 - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j)
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin $$
\Theta(\vec{\xi})=|\xi_2|^3\Re q_1^2 - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j).
$$\DIFaddend 

\end{lemma}
\begin{proof}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{A simple computation shows that, over }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{On the region }\DIFaddend $V$, \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{a direct computation yields
}\DIFaddend $$
|\nabla_\xi (\phi_0(\xi)-\phi_0(\xi_1))| = 3|\xi^2-\xi_1^2|\ge 3\delta^2\max\{|\xi|^2,|\xi_1|^2\},\quad |\nabla_\xi (\phi_E(\xi)-\phi_E(\xi_1))|\lesssim 1.
$$
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{In particular, since $|\xi_1|>\frac{1}{\delta}$, }%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < |\nabla_{\xi} \Theta|\gtrsim 3\delta^2\max\{|\xi|^2,|\xi_1|^2\} - 1 \gtrsim 2\delta^2\max\{|\xi|^2,|\xi_1|^2\}.
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Combined with the lower bound $|\xi_1|>1/\delta$, this gives
}$$
|\nabla_{\xi} \Theta|\gtrsim 3\delta^2\max\{|\xi|^2,|\xi_1|^2\} - 1 \gtrsim 2\delta^2\max\{|\xi|^2,|\xi_1|^2\},
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{proving (i).
}\DIFaddend 

\noi We now \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{prove }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{turn to }\DIFaddend (ii). \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Observe that, over }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The two ingredients driving the argument are (a) the comparability $|\xi_1|\le 2|\xi_2|$ on }\DIFaddend $U$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$|\xi_1|\le 2|\xi_2|$ and $\frac{E}{|\xi|^2}<\delta^2$. Define
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{which makes $|\xi_2|$ the natural unit of length, and (b) the perturbative smallness $|E|/|\xi_2|^2<\delta^2$ of the energy term. We exploit them through the rescaling
}\DIFaddend $$
p_j=\frac{\xi_j}{|\xi_2|},\quad j=\emptyset, 1,\dots, k,
$$
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and write
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \Theta=|\xi_2|^3\left(\phi_0(p) - \sum_{j=1}^k \phi_0(p_j) - \frac{E}{|\xi_2|^2}\left(\phi_E(p) - \sum_{j=1}^k \phi_E(p_j)\right)\right).
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{which puts $\Theta$ into the form
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:Theta_rescaled}
\Theta=|\xi_2|^3\left(\phi_0(p) - \sum_{j=1}^k \phi_0(p_j) - \frac{E}{|\xi_2|^2}\left(\phi_E(p) - \sum_{j=1}^k \phi_E(p_j)\right)\right).
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Setting $c=\sum_{j=2}^kp_k=p-p_1$ and $p_1'=c^{\frac{1}{2}}\left(p_1+\frac{c}{2}\right)$, we observe that, over $U$, $c\in C:=\{c\in\CC: 1/3<|c|<3\}$ and }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{A short manipulation, using $c=\sum_{j=2}^k p_j=p-p_1$ and the shifted variable $p_1'=c^{\frac{1}{2}}\bigl(p_1+\tfrac{c}{2}\bigr)$, identifies the principal part:
}$$
\phi_0(p)-\phi_0(p_1) - \phi_0(c) = 3\Re (p_1')^2.
$$
\DIFadd{The pieces $\phi_0(c)$ and $\sum_{j\ge 2}\phi_0(p_j)$ depend only on $p_2,\dots,p_k$, so they will eventually be reabsorbed into $\sum \phi(\xi_j)$ on the right of \eqref{eq:Theta_rescaled} once we revert to $\xi$-variables. The remaining variable $c$ ranges over the compact annulus $C:=\{c\in\CC: 1/3<|c|<3\}$, and the bound }\DIFaddend $|p_1'|<4\delta$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. A trivial computation gives
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \phi_0(p)-\phi_0(p_1) = 3\Re (p_1')^2.
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{holds throughout $U$.
}

\DIFadd{It is convenient to package the energy contribution as a parameter:
}$$
\varepsilon=\frac{E}{|\xi_2|^2},\qquad |\varepsilon|<\delta^2.
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Next, consider the function
$F:\CC^2\times \R\to \R$ defined as
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < F(p_1', c, \varepsilon) = 3\Re (p_1')^2 - \varepsilon \left(\phi_E(p_1+c) - \phi_E(p_1)\right).
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{With this choice, the function
}$$
F(p_1', c, \varepsilon) = 3\Re (p_1')^2 - \varepsilon \bigl(\phi_E(p_1+c) - \phi_E(p_1)\bigr)
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Fix }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{becomes the object on which the Morse normal form is to be applied. Pick a reference point }\DIFaddend $c_0\in C$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{By an application of Morse 's }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{At $\varepsilon=0$, the map $p_1'\mapsto F(p_1', c_0, 0)$ has an isolated critical point at $p_1'=0$ whose real Hessian has signature $(1,1)$. Invoking the Morse }\DIFaddend lemma with parameters\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < [%%%
\DIFdel{CITE}%DIFDELCMD < ]%%%
\DIFdel{, there exist $\delta,\delta'>0$ such that, for $|c-c_0| + |\varepsilon|<\delta$, there exists a change of coordinates $\varphi_{c,\varepsilon}:B_{4\delta}(0)\to B_{\delta'}(0)$}\DIFdelend , \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{in the form available in H\"ormander, }\emph{\DIFadd{The Analysis of Linear Partial Differential Operators}}\DIFadd{, vol.~I, Lemma~C.6.1 (or Duistermaat, }\emph{\DIFadd{Fourier Integral Operators}}\DIFadd{, Section~3.4), we obtain radii $\eta(c_0),\eta'(c_0)>0$ and a smooth family $\varphi_{c,\varepsilon}:B_{\eta(c_0)}(0)\to B_{\eta'(c_0)}(0)$ of diffeomorphisms }\DIFaddend $\varphi_{c,\varepsilon}(p_1')=q_1$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, such that}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < F(p_1', c, \epsilon) = \Re q_1^2
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{such that, for $|c-c_0|+|\varepsilon|<\eta(c_0)$,
}$$
F(p_1', c, \varepsilon) = \Re q_1^2,\qquad |\det D_{p_1'}\varphi_{c,\varepsilon}|\sim 1.
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and $|\det D^2_{p_1} \varphi_{c,\varepsilon}|\sim 1$. Since $C$ is a compact set, $\delta, \delta'$ can be chosen independently of $c_0$ (and therefore of $k$) }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The next step is to make the radii independent of $c$ via compactness. The family $\{|c-c_0|<\eta(c_0)\}_{c_0\in C}$ covers the compact annulus $C$, so we can extract a finite subcover indexed by $c_0^{(1)},\dots,c_0^{(N)}$ and define
}$$
\delta=\min_{1\le i\le N}\eta(c_0^{(i)}),\qquad \delta'=\min_{1\le i\le N}\eta'(c_0^{(i)}).
$$
\DIFadd{After shrinking $\delta$ further to ensure $\delta^2<\delta$, the constants depend on $E$ (through the upper bound $|E|<1$) but neither on the residual variables $p_2,\dots,p_k$ nor on the height~$k$ of the tree}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Returning to $\Theta$,
we can now write
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \Theta = |\xi_2|^3 F\left(p_1', c, \frac{E}{|\xi_2|^2}\right) - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j) =  |\xi_2|^3\Re q_1^2 - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j) 
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Going back to the original coordinates,
}$$
\Theta = |\xi_2|^3 F\left(p_1', c, \varepsilon\right) - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j) =  |\xi_2|^3\Re q_1^2 - \sum_{j=2}^k \phi(\xi_j).
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and the map $\varphi$ which takes $\xi_1$ into $q_1$ satisfies \eqref{eq:nondeg}. The proof is finished}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The Jacobian \eqref{eq:nondeg} of the resulting map $\varphi:\xi_1\mapsto q_1$ follows from chaining the rescaling $\xi_1=|\xi_2|p_1$ with the unit-Jacobian estimate $|\det D_{p_1'}\varphi_{c,\varepsilon}|\sim 1$}\DIFaddend .
\end{proof}
\DIFaddbegin 

\DIFaddend \begin{remark}
By trivial permutations, the conclusions of Lemma \ref{lem:prop_resonance} also hold for other pairings of frequencies.
\end{remark}

For convenience, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{compile }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{record }\DIFaddend the pointwise estimates for the multipliers $\mul_\ell(\TT)$, $\ell=1,\dots,5$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of }\DIFaddend Lemma \ref{LEM:wint} in the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{next }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{following }\DIFaddend lemma, whose proof is immediate.

\begin{lemma}\DIFaddbegin \label{lem:pointwise_multipliers}
\DIFaddend Given $\xi_1,\xi_2\in\CC$ and $\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2$,
$$
|\Psi_0(\<1>)|\lesssim |\xi\xi_1\xi_2|,\quad  |\Psi_E(\<1>)|\lesssim \min_{j=\emptyset, 1,2}|\xi_j|,\quad |K|\lesssim \frac{1}{|\xi_1||\xi_2|}.
$$
If $|\xi|\gtrsim 1$, then $|\Psi(\<1>)|\lesssim |\xi\xi_1\xi_2|$.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}[Proof of Proposition \ref{prop:bourgL2}]
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We split the proof into several steps , depending on each typeof nonlinear term and on the length of the underlying tree }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The seven steps that follow are arranged primarily by tree type $\ell$ and, within each type, by whether the length $j$ falls below or above the smallest value for which the cluster of $\star$ is entirely interior to }\DIFaddend $\TT$.
\DIFaddbegin 

\DIFaddend \medskip

\noi\textit{Step 1. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend I\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $j=1$, $\TT=\<1>$: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_bi}-(ii)}\DIFaddend .} The \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{only nontrivial Type $\I$ term is when $\TT=\<1>$. The corresponding multiplier can be controlled as
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{bilinear estimate at $j=1$ is the only one not subsumed by Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri}; we split the multiplier $\mul_1(\<1>)$ into two pieces and feed each into Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_bi}-(ii) with $\beta=1$, the residual $\beta=1$ being relaxed to $\beta<1$ at the end via Lemma~\ref{lem:eta1}.
We have
}\DIFaddend $$
|\mul_1(\<1>)|\lesssim |\xi|\ind_A + K|\Psi_E(\<1>)|\ind_{A^c} \lesssim |\xi|\ind_A + \frac{\ind_{A^c}}{\max_{\bul\in\{\emptyset, 1, 2\}}|\xi_\bul|}.
$$
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Suppose, without }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Without }\DIFaddend loss of generality, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{that }\DIFdelend $|\xi_1|\gtrsim |\xi_2|$.
For the first term, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{since $|\xi_2|\lesssim 1$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$|\xi_2|\lesssim 1/\delta$ on $A$ }\DIFaddend and $|\partial_{\xi_2}\Psi(\<1>)|\gtrsim |\xi|^2$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we have
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_\xi \int_A \frac{|\xi|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s}} \ind_{|\Psi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_2 \lesssim \sup_\xi \int_{|\zeta_2|<1/\delta}  \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} d\phi d\zeta_2 \lesssim \delta^{-1}M
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{so that
}$$
\sup_\xi \int_A \frac{|\xi|^2\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s}} \ind_{|\Psi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_2 \lesssim \sup_\xi \int_{|\zeta_2|<1/\delta}  \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} \,d\phi\, d\zeta_2 \lesssim \delta^{-1}M.
$$\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and the estimate follows from Lemma}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Lemma~\ref{lem:eta1} converts the $\delta^{-1}M$ on the right-hand side into $\delta^{-1}M^\beta$ for some $\beta<1$ (the $\delta^{-1}$ is harmless as it carries no $M$-dependence), so Lemma~}\DIFaddend \ref{lem:fre_bi}-(ii) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{together with Lemma \ref{lem:eta1}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{applies}\DIFaddend .

For the second term, %DIF <  if any frequency is $\lesssim 1$, say $\xi_2$, then
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  \sup_\xi \int_A \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s}} \ind_{|\Psi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_2 \lesssim 1.
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  Assuming now that all frequencies are large, 
we may assume that $\xi\not\simeq \pm \xi_2$ (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{if this is not true, then }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{otherwise }\DIFaddend $\xi_1\not\simeq \pm \xi_2$ and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the proof follows from switching }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{we swap the roles of }\DIFaddend $\xi$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{with }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and }\DIFaddend $\xi_1$), \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{which implies }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{so }\DIFaddend that $|\partial_{\xi_2}\Psi(\<1>)|\gtrsim |\xi|^2$. Then
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_\xi \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s}} \ind_{|\Psi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_2 \lesssim \sup_\xi \int \frac{1}{|\zeta_2|^{4+2s-}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}d\phi d\zeta_2 \lesssim M
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin $$
\sup_\xi \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s}} \ind_{|\Psi(\<1>)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_2 \lesssim \sup_\xi \int \frac{1}{|\zeta_2|^{4+2s-}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}\,d\phi\, d\zeta_2 \lesssim M,
$$\DIFaddend 
and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we apply once again Lemmas}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Lemmas~}\DIFaddend \ref{lem:fre_bi}-(ii) and\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\ref{lem:eta1}. This concludes the proof for type $\I$ terms}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~\ref{lem:eta1} apply once more.
}

\DIFadd{The output is the bound $\delta^{-1}$, weaker than the uniform $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}=\delta^{-4s-5}$ (cf.\ Remark~\ref{rmk:exponent_optimal}), but with the explicit $\delta^{-1}$ that controls the geometric series in $j$}\DIFaddend .

\medskip

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{From now on, the proof of \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2} for $\ell=2,\dots, 5$ follows from Lemma\ref{lem:fre_tri}, with an appropriate choice of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{For Types II--V (i.e.\ $\ell=2,\dots,5$) the workhorse switches from Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_bi} to Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri}, whose flexibility in choosing the splitting }\DIFaddend set $B$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, and Lemma\ref{lem:eta1}}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is essential. Lemma~\ref{lem:eta1} is then applied at the very end of each step}\DIFaddend .

\medskip

\noi\textit{Step 2. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend II\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\ell=2$, $j\ge 2$: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri} with $B=\{\star 2\}$}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{For }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The Type~II multiplier carries an extra inverse weight at the parent leaf of $\star$. Choosing $B=\{\star 2\}$ splits the integrations so that resonance is traded only against $\xi_{\star 2}$ (yielding $M$), while each of the $j-2$ remaining internal nodes contributes a factor $\delta^{2s+2}$ via the small-frequency restriction $|\xi_{\bul 2}|\lesssim 1/\delta$; the cumulative effect is $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-2)}M$.
We have, for }\DIFaddend $\TT\in \Tr_j$, $j\ge 2$,
$$
|\mul_2(\TT)| \lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^s}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{s}\jap{\xi_{\star2}}^{s}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{s+1}}\prod_{\substack{\bul\in\TT^0\\\bul\neq \star, \pb(\star)}} \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}^{s+1}}.
$$
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{As we are in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{On }\DIFaddend $A_\star$, we \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{can assume that $|\xi_{\star2}|\lesssim 1$. Concerning the other frequencies, the }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{have $|\xi_{\star2}|\lesssim 1/\delta$. The }\DIFaddend worst-case scenario occurs when $\xi_{\star1}$ corresponds to the largest frequency \DIFdelbegin \footnote{\DIFdel{We can suppose this because we are not going to use the specific tree structure any further.}}%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{footnote}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{.Then, for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{(the specific tree structure plays no further role).}\footnote{\DIFadd{We can suppose this because the bound is symmetric in the leaves once we have isolated $\star$.}} \DIFadd{For }\DIFaddend $\xi$ and $\xi_{\bul2}$, $\bul\in \TT^0\setminus\{\star1\}$, fixed,
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}
%DIFDELCMD < \int |\xi_{\star1}|^2\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{\star2} \lesssim \int \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} d\phi d\zeta_{\star2} \lesssim M.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}
\int |\xi_{\star1}|^2\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{\star2} \lesssim \int \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} \,d\phi\, d\zeta_{\star2} \lesssim M.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
On the other hand, for \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\xi_{\star1}. \xi_{\star2}$ fixed, we do not make any use of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\xi_{\star1},\xi_{\star2}$ fixed, }\DIFaddend the resonance restriction \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{:
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < &\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{2s+2}}\cdot\prod_{\substack{\bul\in\TT^0\\\bul\neq \star, \pb(\star)}} \frac{d\xi_{\bul2}}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}^2\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}^{2s+2}}\cdot \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi\\\lesssim & \int\left(\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}d\xi}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{2s+2}}\right)\prod_{\substack{\bul\in\TT^0\\\bul\neq \star, \pb(\star)}} \frac{d\xi_{\bul2}}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}^2\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}^{2s+2}} \lesssim \delta^{(2s+2)(j-2)}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is not used:
}\begin{align*}
&\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{2s+2}}\cdot\prod_{\substack{\bul\in\TT^0\\\bul\neq \star, \pb(\star)}} \frac{d\xi_{\bul2}}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}^2\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}^{2s+2}}\cdot \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\, d\xi\\
\lesssim {}& \int\left(\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}\,d\xi}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{2s+2-}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{2s+2}}\right)\prod_{\substack{\bul\in\TT^0\\\bul\neq \star, \pb(\star)}} \frac{d\xi_{\bul2}}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}^2\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}^{2s+2}}  \lesssim \delta^{(2s+2)(j-2)}.
\end{align*}\DIFaddend 
\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Plugging both bounds into Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri} and then upgrading via Lemma~\ref{lem:eta1} delivers \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2}.
}\DIFaddend 

\medskip

\noi \textit{Step 3. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend IV\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\ell=4$}\DIFaddend , $j=2$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\TT=\<21>$: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri} with $B=\{11\}$, supported by Lemma~\ref{lem:prop_resonance}}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{It is convenient to consider the case $\pb(\star)=\emptyset$ separately. If so, then we can assume that }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{With $j=2$ the only tree is $\TT=\<21>$. Both quantities \eqref{eq:type4interp1}--\eqref{eq:type4interp2} below are estimated by integrating along the resonance level set; the genuinely delicate situation is the stationary one (Case~B2 below), which is resolved by invoking the Morse change of coordinates of Lemma~\ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii).
With }\DIFaddend $\TT=\<21>$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and 
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{,
}\DIFaddend \begin{equation}
\label{typeIVmult2}
|\mul_4(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s+1}}{\jap{\xi_{11}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_2}^s}.
\end{equation}
The worst-case scenario corresponds to $|\xi_2|\ge |\xi|\ge |\xi_{11}|\ge |\xi_{12}|$. The proof \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{follows deriving bounds on
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:type4interp1}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi,\xi_{12},\alpha} \int |\xi|^{1-} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\xi_{11}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{proceeds by bounding
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:type4interp1}
\sup_{\xi,\xi_{12},\alpha} \int |\xi|^{1-} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\,d\xi_{11}
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
and
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:type4interp2}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi_2,\xi_{11},\alpha} \int \frac{|\xi|^{1+}}{\jap{\xi_{12}}^{4s+4}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\xi_{12}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:type4interp2}
\sup_{\xi_2,\xi_{11},\alpha} \int \frac{|\xi|^{1+}}{\jap{\xi_{12}}^{4s+4}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\,d\xi_{12}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case A.} $\xi\not\simeq \pm \xi_{12}$ and $\xi_2\not\simeq \pm \xi_{11}$.

\noi For $\xi, \xi_{12}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we bound
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVest1}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:type4interp1}\lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi_2|^{1+}}\ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}d\phi d\zeta_{11} \lesssim M.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVest1}
\eqref{eq:type4interp1}\lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi_2|^{1+}}\ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}\,d\phi\, d\zeta_{11} \lesssim M.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
For $\xi_2, \xi_{11}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVest2}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:type4interp2} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{12}}^{4s+4}|\xi|^{1-}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\phi d\zeta_{12} \lesssim M.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVest2}
\eqref{eq:type4interp2} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{12}}^{4s+4}|\xi|^{1-}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\,d\phi\, d\zeta_{12} \lesssim M.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi
\textbf{Case B.} $\xi\simeq \pm \xi_{12}$ or $\xi_2\simeq \pm \xi_{11}$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Observe that this implies that all }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Then all four }\DIFaddend frequencies are comparable\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and thus
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, so that
}\DIFaddend $$
|\mul_4(\TT)|\lesssim |\xi|^{-1-2s}.
$$

\smallskip
\noi
\textbf{Case B1.} Up to permutations, the conditions of Case A are met\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. It suffices to follow }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{; it suffices to repeat }\DIFaddend the arguments therein.

\smallskip
\noi
\textbf{Case B2.} \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We have three frequencies which are equal (}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Three of the frequencies are equal }\DIFaddend up to a sign\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{)}\DIFdelend , say $\xi_2\simeq  \xi_{11} \simeq \pm \xi_{12}$. If the sign is \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the same, then
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \xi_2\simeq \xi_{11}\simeq \xi_{12} \simeq \frac{\xi}{3}.
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{positive, then
}$$
\xi_2\simeq \xi_{11}\simeq \xi_{12} \simeq \tfrac{\xi}{3}.
$$\DIFaddend 
For $\xi_2, \xi_{11}$ fixed \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, }\DIFdelend we proceed as in Case A (\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{since the nonstationary condition is still satisfied}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the non-stationarity condition still holds}\DIFaddend ). For $\xi, \xi_{12}$ fixed, we apply Lemma \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{to estimate
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:type4interp1}\lesssim \int_{|q_1|\ll 1} |\xi_2|^{3-}\ind_{||\xi|^3\Re q_1^2 - \Tilde{\alpha}|<M} dq_1 \lesssim M^{1^-}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{(with $\xi_1$ replaced by $\xi_{11}$, $\xi$ replaced by $\xi-\xi_{12}$, and parameters rescaled by $|\xi_2|$) to obtain
}\begin{align}
\eqref{eq:type4interp1}\lesssim \int_{|q_1|\ll 1} |\xi_2|^{3-}\ind_{||\xi|^3\Re q_1^2 - \widetilde\alpha|<M} \,dq_1 \lesssim M^{1-}.
\end{align}\DIFaddend 

%DIF <  For $\xi_2, \xi_{11}$ fixed, we proceed as in \eqref{eq:typeIVest2}. For $\xi, \xi_{12}$ fixed, we define
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  p_\bul = \frac{\xi_\bul}{|\xi|}, \qquad\bul=\emptyset, 2, 11, 12.
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  The resonance function can be written as
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  \Psi(\TT)=|\xi|^3 \left(P(p_2)-\frac{E}{|\xi|^2}R(p_2)\right),\quad P(p_2)=\Re(p^3-p_2^3-p_{11}^3-p_{12}^3)
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  R(p_2)=\Re\left(p^3-\frac{p_2^3}{|p_2|
%DIF <  ^2}-\frac{p_{11}^3}{|p_{11}|^2}-\frac{p_{12}^3}{|p_{12}|^2}\right) 
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  Consider the function
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  F(p_2;p, p_{12}, \varepsilon)= P(p_2) + \varepsilon R(p_2)
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  For $\epsilon =0$, we are near a nondegenerate stationary point $p_2^0$ of $F$. Then, by Morse's lemma with parameters, for $\varepsilon>0$ small, there exist $\lambda_1, \lambda_2\in \{\pm1\}$ such that
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  F(p_2;p, p_{12}, \varepsilon) = c(p, p_{12}, \varepsilon) + \lambda_1 q_2^2 + \lambda_2 r_2^2, \quad q_2,r_2\in \R, \quad |q_2|+|r_2|\ll 1.
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  Then, for $\epsilon=-E/|\xi|^2$, we bound 
%DIF <  \begin{align*}
%DIF <  \eqref{eq:type4interp2}\lesssim &\int |\xi|^{3-} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}dp_{2}\\\lesssim &\int_{|q_2|+|r_2|\ll 1}|\xi|^{3-} \ind_{|c(p, p_{12}, \varepsilon) + \lambda_1 q_2^2 + \lambda_2 r_2^2-\alpha|<M}dq_{2}dr_2 \lesssim M^{1-}
%DIF <  \end{align*}
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend Finally, if $\xi_2\simeq \xi_{11}\simeq-\xi_{12}$, then $\xi\simeq -\xi_{12}$. In this case, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend both \eqref{eq:type4interp1} and \eqref{eq:type4interp2} \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we proceed using }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{are handled by }\DIFaddend Lemma \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii) as above.

\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The case $j\ge 3$, handled next, differs only in that the $j-3$ internal nodes outside the cluster of $\star$ contribute free $\delta^{2s+2}$ factors via $\Psi_E$.
}

\DIFaddend \medskip

\noi \textit{Step 4. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend IV\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend , \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$j\ge3$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\ell=4$, $j\ge 3$: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri}, with the $j-3$ free integrations accumulating $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Denote }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{At lengths $j\ge 3$ the tree has $j-3$ additional internal nodes outside the cluster of $\star$. Each contributes an unrestricted integration on $|\xi_{\bul 2}|\lesssim 1/\delta$, and the budget $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$ in the final bound comes entirely from these. The dichotomy of Step~3 -- non-stationary (Case~A) versus stationary (Case~B) -- is reproduced verbatim at the level of \eqref{eq:IVinterp1}--\eqref{eq:IVinterp2}.
Set }\DIFaddend $\circ=\gb(\star)$. Then
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVmult}
%DIFDELCMD < |\mul_4(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s}}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ12}}^{s}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:typeIVmult}
|\mul_4(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s}}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ12}}^{s}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
We focus on the worst-case scenario $|\xi_{\circ12}|\ge |\xi_{\circ 2}|\ge |\xi_{\circ 111}| \ge |\xi_{\circ 112}| \ge |\xi|$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{We then consider the quantities
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:IVinterp1}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi_{\circ111}, \xi_{\circ12}}\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{1+2s}}\left(\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2}\right) \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\xi d\xi_{\circ112}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Consider
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:IVinterp1}
\sup_{\xi_{\circ111}, \xi_{\circ12}}\int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{1+2s}}\left(\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2}\right) \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\,d\xi\, d\xi_{\circ112}
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
and
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:IVinterp2}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi, \xi_{\circ2}, \xi_{\circ112}, \xi_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ}, }\int \frac{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{1+}}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{\circ111}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:IVinterp2}
\sup_{\xi, \xi_{\circ2}, \xi_{\circ112}, \xi_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ}}\int \frac{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{1+}}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{\circ111}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case A.} $\xi_{\circ12}\not\simeq \pm \xi_{\circ111}$ and $\xi_{\circ2}\not\simeq \pm \xi_{\circ112}$.

\noi For $\xi_{\circ12}, \xi_{\circ111}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we estimate
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:IVinterp1}\lesssim & \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{3+2s}}\left(\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2}\right) \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}d\xi d\zeta_{\circ112}\lesssim \delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}M
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align*}
\eqref{eq:IVinterp1}\lesssim & \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\circ12}|^{3+2s}}\left(\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq\circ} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2}\right) \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}\,d\xi\, d\zeta_{\circ112}\lesssim \delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}M,
\end{align*}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{while}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{where the $j-3$ factors of $\delta^{2s+2}$ originate from the $|\xi_{\bul 2}|\lesssim 1/\delta$ constraints associated with each of the $j-3$ internal vertices not lying above $\circ$.
Similarly}\DIFaddend , for $\xi, \xi_{\circ2}, \xi_{\circ112}$ and $\xi_{\bul\in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \circ}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{we bound
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align*}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:IVinterp2} \lesssim & \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{2s+2}|\xi_{\circ2}|^{1-}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\phi d\zeta_{\circ111} \lesssim M
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align*}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align*}
\eqref{eq:IVinterp2} \lesssim & \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{2s+2}|\xi_{\circ2}|^{1-}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\, d\phi\, d\zeta_{\circ111} \lesssim M.
\end{align*}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi
\textbf{Case B.} $\xi_{\circ12}\simeq \pm \xi_{\circ111}$ or $\xi_{\circ2}\simeq \pm \xi_{\circ112}$.

\noi \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{It suffices to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{We }\DIFaddend proceed as in the corresponding Case B \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of }\DIFaddend Step 3, applying if necessary the change of coordinates of Lemma \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii)\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. We leave the details to the interested reader}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{; the $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$ factor again arises from the $j-3$ free integrations}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \medskip
\DIFaddend \noi\textit{Step 5. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend III\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\ell=3$, $j\ge 2$: reduction to Type~IV (Steps~3--4)}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Given }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Type~III is not analysed on its own: the bound on $\mul_3(\TT)$ carries an extra inverse weight $\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{-(s+1)}$ relative to $\mul_4(\TT)$, hence any frequency-restricted estimate valid for the latter applies a fortiori to the former.
Indeed, given }\DIFaddend $\TT\in \Tr_j$, $j\ge 2$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{since }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{the estimate }\DIFaddend $|\Psi_E(\star)|\lesssim |\xi_\star|$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{,
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < |\mul_3(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s}}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star2}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{s+1}}\prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)}\frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul}}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^{s+1}}
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{yields
}$$
|\mul_3(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s}}{\jap{\xi_{\star1}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star2}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{s+1}}\prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)}\frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul}}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^{s+1}}.
$$\DIFaddend 
If $j=2$, this is a stronger bound than \eqref{typeIVmult2}.
If $j\ge 3$, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{taking }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{with }\DIFaddend $\circ=\gb(\star)$, this estimate can be rewritten as
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < |\mul_3(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^s}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ1}}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \circ}\frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul}}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^{s+1}}
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin $$
|\mul_3(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^s}{\jap{\xi_{\circ111}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ112}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\circ1}}\jap{\xi_{\circ2}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \circ}\frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul}}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^{s+1}},
$$\DIFaddend 
which is smaller than the bound \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \eqref{eq:typeIVmult}. In \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{any case , the estimate for type $\III$ terms is reducible to that for type $\IV$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{either case the Type~III estimate follows from the proof of Steps~3 and~4 verbatim}\DIFaddend .

%DIF <  If $|\xi_\star|\lesssim |\xi_{\pb(\star)}|$, then this can be controlled as in Type $\IV$ terms. We therefore assume that $|\xi_\star|\gg |\xi_{\pb(\star)}|$, which implies that $\xi_{\star1}+\xi_{\star2}\simeq -\xi_{\sbf(\star)}$. Assuming, without loss of generality, that $|\xi_{\star1}|\ge |\xi_{\star2}|\ge |\xi_{\sbf(\star)}|$, we must have $\xi_{\sbf(\star)}\not\simeq \pm \xi_{\star1}$. Moreover, the worst-case scenario occurs when all three frequencies are $\gtrsim |\xi|$.
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
%DIF <  For $\xi_{\star1}, \xi_{\star2}, \xi_{\sbf(\star)}$ fixed,
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\star1}|^{2s+2}}\left(\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}}\right)d\xi \lesssim \delta^{(2s+2)j}.
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  On the other hand, given $\xi, \xi_{\bul\in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)}$,
%DIF <  $$
%DIF <  \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\star2}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\xi_{\star2}d\xi_{\sbf(\star)}
%DIF <  $$
%DIFDELCMD < 

%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdelend \medskip
\noi\textit{Step 6. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend V\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\ell=5$}\DIFaddend , $j=3$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\TT=\<33>$: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri}, supported by Lemma~\ref{lem:prop_resonance}}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Once again, we must consider the case $\star=\emptyset$ separately. In this situation, }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{At $j=3$, Type~V is realised by the single tree }\DIFaddend $\TT=\<33>$\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and the corresponding multiplier can be controlled as
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < |\mul_5(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s+1}}{\jap{\xi_{11}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{21}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{s+1}}
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, whose multiplier involves four leaves rather than three. The bounds for the two integrals \eqref{eq:Vinterp1}--\eqref{eq:Vinterp2} extend those of Step~3 by one resonance-free integration, again resolved either by non-stationarity (Case~A) or, on the stationary stratum, by Lemma~\ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii) (Case~B2).
With $\TT=\<33>$,
}$$
|\mul_5(\TT)|\lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^{s+1}}{\jap{\xi_{11}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{21}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{s+1}}.
$$\DIFaddend 
The worst-case scenario occurs \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{when }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{for }\DIFaddend $|\xi|\ge |\xi_{11}|\ge |\xi_{12}|\ge |\xi_{21}|\ge |\xi_{22}|$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, }\DIFaddend and we consider
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the quantities
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp1}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi, \xi_{12}, \xi_{22}}\int |\xi|^{1-} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{21}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp1}
\sup_{\xi, \xi_{12}, \xi_{22}}\int |\xi|^{1-} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{21}
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
and
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp2}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi_{11}, \xi_{21}}\int \frac{1}{|\xi|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{12}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{21}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{12}d\xi_{22}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp2}
\sup_{\xi_{11}, \xi_{21}}\int \frac{1}{|\xi|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{12}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{21}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} \,d\xi_{12}\,d\xi_{22}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case A.} $\xi\not\simeq \pm \xi_{12}$ and $\xi_{11}\not\simeq \pm\xi_{21}$.

\noi For $\xi, \xi_{12}, \xi_{22}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:estVinterp1}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:Vinterp1} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi|^{1+}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} d\phi  d\zeta_{21} \lesssim M 
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:estVinterp1}
\eqref{eq:Vinterp1} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi|^{1+}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M} \,d\phi\,  d\zeta_{21} \lesssim M.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and, for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{For }\DIFaddend $\xi_{11}, \xi_{21}$ fixed,
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:estVinterp2}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:Vinterp2} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi_{11}|^{1-}\jap{\zeta_{12}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{4s+4}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}  d\phi d\zeta_{21}d\xi_{22} \lesssim M.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:estVinterp2}
\eqref{eq:Vinterp2} \lesssim \int \frac{1}{|\xi_{11}|^{1-}\jap{\zeta_{12}}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_{22}}^{4s+4}} \ind_{|\phi-\alpha|<M}\, d\phi\, d\zeta_{21}\,d\xi_{22} \lesssim M.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case B.} $\xi\simeq \pm \xi_{12}$ or $\xi_{11}\simeq \pm\xi_{21}$. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{This implies in particularthat }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{In particular, }\DIFaddend $|\xi|\sim |\xi_{21}|$. We split further\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{into two cases}\DIFdelend :

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case B1.} Up to \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{permutations of $\xi, \xi_{11}, \xi_{12}$ and $\xi_{21}$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{a permutation of $\xi, \xi_{11}, \xi_{12}, \xi_{21}$}\DIFaddend , the conditions of Case A are met\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{(in which case we proceed as above)}\DIFdelend .

\smallskip
\noi\textbf{Case B2.} The frequencies \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\xi_{11}, \xi_{12}$ and $\xi_{21}$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\xi_{11}, \xi_{12}, \xi_{21}$ }\DIFaddend are equal up to a sign. \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{In this case, up to permutation of the frequencies, we can suppose that
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Up to permutation we may assume
}\DIFaddend $$
\xi \not\simeq \xi_{12} \quad \mbox{and}\quad \xi_{11}\not\simeq -\xi_{21}.
$$
For $\xi, \xi_{12}, \xi_{22}$ fixed, either \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\xi_{11} \not\simeq -\xi_{31}$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\xi_{11} \not\simeq -\xi_{21}$ }\DIFaddend (and we bound \eqref{eq:Vinterp1} as in \eqref{eq:estVinterp1}) or \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\xi_{11}\simeq -\xi_{31}$}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\xi_{11}\simeq -\xi_{21}$}\DIFaddend . In the latter \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{case, by }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{sub-case, }\DIFaddend Lemma \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii) \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{,
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}
%DIFDELCMD < \eqref{eq:Vinterp1} \lesssim \int |\xi|^{3-}\ind_{||\xi|^2\Re q_1^2 - \Tilde{\alpha}|<M} dq_1 \lesssim M^{1-}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{yields
}\begin{equation}
\eqref{eq:Vinterp1} \lesssim \int |\xi|^{3-}\ind_{||\xi|^2\Re q_1^2 - \widetilde\alpha|<M} \,dq_1 \lesssim M^{1-}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
For $\xi_{11}, \xi_{21}$ fixed \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we split analogouslyin the nonstationary and stationary cases, arguing as in \eqref{eq:estVinterp2} or using Lemma}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{we argue analogously, splitting between the non-stationary case (handled by \eqref{eq:estVinterp2}) and the stationary one (handled by Lemma~}\DIFaddend \ref{lem:prop_resonance}-(ii)\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{).
}

\DIFadd{In the next step we treat Type~V with $j\ge 4$, where the additional internal nodes contribute $j-3$ free integrations and the new leaf $\xi_{\sbf(\star)}$ requires an extra resonance-free integration that is absorbed by the $|\xi_{\star11}|^{2}$ weight in $\mul_5$}\DIFaddend .

\medskip
\noi\textit{Step 7. Type\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend V\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{estimate}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $\ell=5$}\DIFaddend , $j\ge 4$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{: workhorse Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri}, with one additional integration absorbed by the $|\xi_{\star 1 1}|^{2}$ weight}\DIFaddend .}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{In this case, the multiplier can be controlled as
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < |\mul_5(\TT)| \lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^s}{\jap{\xi_{\star11}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star21}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star22}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)} \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}\jap{\xi_\bul}^{s+1}}
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{For lengths $j\ge 4$, Type~V exhibits a structural feature that has no counterpart in Step~4: the node $\sbf(\star)$, which is internal for Type~IV trees, becomes a leaf of $\TT_5$ and thus contributes a free integration variable. The compensation is built into $\mul_5$ via an extra inverse weight $|\xi_{\star 11}|^{-2}$ absent from $\mul_4$, and below we trace how this weight precisely absorbs the new variable while leaving the $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$ accounting of Step~4 intact.
The multiplier is now
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:mul5_high_j}
|\mul_5(\TT)| \lesssim \frac{\jap{\xi}^s}{\jap{\xi_{\star11}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star12}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star21}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\star22}}^{s+1}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{s+1}} \prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)} \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}\jap{\xi_\bul}^{s+1}}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
In the worst-case scenario, $|\xi_{\star11}|\ge|\xi_{\star12}|\ge|\xi_{\star21}|\ge|\xi_{\star22}|\ge|\xi_{\sbf(\star)}|\ge |\xi|$. We consider
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp3}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi_{\star11}, \xi_{\star21}, \xi_{\sbf(\star)}} \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\star11}|^{1+2s}}\prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}}\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}d\xi d\xi_{\star22}
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp3}
\sup_{\xi_{\star11}, \xi_{\star21}, \xi_{\sbf(\star)}} \int \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{|\xi_{\star11}|^{1+2s}}\prod_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)} \frac{d\xi_\bul}{\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\bul)}}^2\jap{\xi_\bul}^{2s+2}}\,\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\,d\xi\, d\xi_{\star22}
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
and
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp4}
%DIFDELCMD < \sup_{\xi, \xi_{\star12}, \xi_{\star22}, \xi_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)}} \int \frac{1}{|\xi_{\star11}|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{\star21}}^{4s+4}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{4s+4}} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M} d\xi_{\star21}d\xi_{\sbf(\star)}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{equation}\label{eq:Vinterp4}
\sup_{\xi, \xi_{\star12}, \xi_{\star22}, \xi_{\bul \in \TT^\infty, \bul\ngeq \pb(\star)}} \int \frac{1}{|\xi_{\star11}|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{\star21}}^{4s+4}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{4s+4}} \ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}\, d\xi_{\star21}\,d\xi_{\sbf(\star)}.
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Notice that \eqref{eq:Vinterp3} corresponds to \eqref{eq:IVinterp1} , while \eqref{eq:Vinterp4} is similar to\eqref{eq:IVinterp2}, with the exception that it has
an extra integration and an extra $|\xi_{\star11}|^2$ weight to compensate. It now suffices to proceed as in Step}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin 

\DIFadd{The quantity \eqref{eq:Vinterp3} is structurally identical to \eqref{eq:IVinterp1} of Step~4: the integration $d\xi$ runs over the resonance level set and produces $M$ as in Case~A of Step~4, while the $j-3$ free integrations on $|\xi_{\bul 2}|\lesssim 1/\delta$ associated with the internal nodes not lying above $\pb(\star)$ accumulate the factor $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}$.
}

\DIFadd{The quantity \eqref{eq:Vinterp4} is the genuine novelty of Step~7. Compared with its Step~4 analogue \eqref{eq:IVinterp2}, it carries }\emph{\DIFadd{one additional integration}} \DIFadd{variable, namely $\xi_{\sbf(\star)}$ (the parent of the cluster of $\star$, which is a leaf in $\TT_5$ but an internal node in $\TT_4$). The compensation comes from a single }\emph{\DIFadd{extra inverse weight}} \DIFadd{$|\xi_{\star 1 1}|^{-2}$ that is present in $\mul_5$ but absent in $\mul_4$: using $|\xi_{\star 1 1}|\ge |\xi_{\sbf(\star)}|$ in the worst-case ordering, one has
}$$
\frac{1}{|\xi_{\star 1 1}|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{\star 2 1}}^{4s+4}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{4s+4}} \lesssim \frac{1}{|\xi_{\star 1 1}|^{1-}\jap{\xi_{\star 2 1}}^{4s+4}\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{4s+2}\,|\xi_{\star11}|^{2}},
$$
\DIFadd{so that the integration in $\xi_{\sbf(\star)}$ converges as $\int\jap{\xi_{\sbf(\star)}}^{-(4s+2)}\,d\xi_{\sbf(\star)}\lesssim 1$ for $s>-1$, and the surviving $|\xi_{\star 1 1}|^{-(3-)}$ together with the resonance restriction $\ind_{|\Psi(\TT)-\alpha|<M}$ on $\xi_{\star 2 1}$ produces the bound $M$ exactly as in Case~A of Step~}\DIFaddend 4. \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{In other words, the extra integration of Step~7 introduces }\emph{\DIFadd{one extra parent node}} \DIFadd{($\sbf(\star)$) compared with Step~4, and the $|\xi_{\star11}|^{2}$ weight in $\mul_5$ supplies precisely the $\delta^{2s+2}$ budget required to absorb it without consuming resonance. The bookkeeping of the remaining $j-3$ free integrations is identical to Step~4, and the end result is again $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)}M$. An application of Lemma~\ref{lem:fre_tri} combined with Lemma~\ref{lem:eta1} closes \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2}.
}

\medskip

\DIFadd{Assembling Steps~1--7 yields, for every $\TT\in\Tr_j$ and every $\ell\in\{1,\dots,5\}$, the estimate \eqref{eq:bourg_bi_l2} with the uniform exponent $\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}$ (cf.\ Remark~\ref{rmk:exponent_optimal}). This is precisely the input absorbed by the contraction argument in Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv}: under the smallness assumption~\eqref{eq:escolhadelta}, the geometric series $\sum_{j\ge 1} C^j \delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1} R^{j+1}$ sums to $O(\delta^{-4s-5}R^2)$, with the dominant contribution coming from the Type-I term.
}\DIFaddend \end{proof}



\section{Proof of the main theorem}\DIFaddbegin \label{sec:lwp}
\DIFaddend 

In this section, we prove Theorem \ref{thm:main_intro}. By a suitable rescaling, it suffices to consider the case $|E|<1$. Throughout this section, we fix $R\gg 1$ and take $\delta>0$ such that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:escolhadelta}
\delta^{2s+2}R\ll 1.
\end{equation}

\begin{proposition}[Local well-posedness for the gauged NV equation]\label{prop:lwp_rnv}
Fix $s>-1$. Given $z_0\in H^s(\R^2)$ with $\|z_0\|_{H^s}<R$, there exist $T=T_{\delta,R}>0$ and a unique
$$
z\in X^{s,\frac{1}{2} +}(0,T)
$$
solution of \eqref{z1} over $(0,T)$ with initial data $z_0$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{While the proof is standard, we sketch the main estimates }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The argument is by Banach fixed point in the standard way; we record the main inequality in order }\DIFaddend to highlight the dependence on $\delta$.

Fix $b=\frac{1}{2}+$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{. Define 
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < B_{R,T}=\left\{ z\in X^{s,b} : \|z\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}\le 2R \right\},
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{and define
}$$
B_{R,T}=\left\{ z\in X^{s,b}_T : \|z\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}\le 2R \right\},
$$\DIFaddend 
endowed with the induced distance, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and
}%DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \Theta[z](t)=U(t)z_0 + \int_0^t U(t-t')\sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  \Ncal_\l(\TT;z)(t')dt'
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{together with the integral map
}$$
\Theta[z](t)=U(t)z_0 + \int_0^t U(t-t')\sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5  \Ncal_\l(\TT;z)(t')\,dt'.
$$\DIFaddend 
Applying the multilinear estimates \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in Proposition \ref{prop:bourgL2} , given }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{of Proposition \ref{prop:bourgL2} and recalling that $|\Tr_j|$ grows only exponentially in $j$ (cf.~\eqref{eq:catalan}), for any }\DIFaddend $z\in B_{R,T}$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{,
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \|\Theta[z]\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)} &\le \|z_0\|_{H^s} + T^{0+}\sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT \in \Tr_j} \sum_{\l=1}^5 C^j\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}\|z\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}^{j+1} \\&\le R + T^{0+}\sum_{j=1}^\infty C^j\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}R^{j+1} \\&\le R+T^{0+}C\delta^{-4s-5}R^2 \le 2R,
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{we obtain
}\begin{align}
\|\Theta[z]\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}
&\le \|z_0\|_{H^s} + T^{0+}\sum_{j=1}^\infty C^j\delta^{(2s+2)(j-3)-1}\|z\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}^{j+1} \\
&\le R + T^{0+}\delta^{-4s-5}\sum_{j=1}^\infty \big(C \,\delta^{2s+2}\, R\big)^{j-1} \cdot C R^2 \\
&\le R + T^{0+} C \,\delta^{-4s-5}\, R^2 \le 2R,
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{for }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{where the geometric series converges thanks to the smallness condition \eqref{eq:escolhadelta} and }\DIFaddend $T=T_{\delta,R}$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{sufficiently small}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{is chosen sufficiently small in the last inequality}\DIFaddend . Using the multilinear structure of the nonlinear terms, an analogous computation yields
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < $$
%DIFDELCMD < \|\Theta[z]-\Theta[z']\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)} \le T^{0+}C\delta^{-4s-5}R\|z-z'\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)} \le \frac{1}{2}\|z-z'\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}.
%DIFDELCMD < $$%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin $$
\|\Theta[z]-\Theta[z']\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)} \le T^{0+}C\delta^{-4s-5}R\|z-z'\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)} \le \tfrac12\|z-z'\|_{X^{s,b}(0,T)}.
$$\DIFaddend 
The result \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{now }\DIFdelend follows from Banach's fixed point theorem.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}\label{remark:persistence}
If $z_0\in H^{s'}(\R^2)$, for some $s'>s$, a standard persistence-of-regularity argument shows that $z\in X^{s',b}(0,T) \hookrightarrow C([0,T]; H^s(\R^2))$.
\end{remark}


Recall the (formal) definition of the gauge transform,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:gauge}
\mathcal{G}_\delta^{-1}[f]=f+\F_{z}^{-1}\left(\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} K\mathbbm{1}_{A^c_\delta}(\xi_1,\xi_2)\widehat{f}(\xi_1)\widehat{f}(\xi_2)d\xi_1\right).
\end{equation}



\begin{lemma}\label{LEM:D}

Consider the map  $\Gc^{-1}$ defined in \eqref{eq:gauge}.

\smallskip



\noi {\rm(i)}
Let $s' \ge s>-1$, $R>0$, $0<\dl \ll R^{-\frac{1}{2s+2}}$, and \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$B_{R}^{s',s}$ given by
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{Bss}
%DIFDELCMD < B^{s',s}_\delta=\left\{ f\in H^{s'}(\R^2): \|f\|_{H^s} \le R \right\}.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$B^{s',s}_R$ be given by
}\begin{align}
\label{Bss}
B^{s',s}_R=\left\{ f\in H^{s'}(\R^2): \|f\|_{H^s} \le R \right\}.
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
Then, there exists \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$0<\epsilon\ll 1$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$0<\eps\ll 1$ }\DIFaddend such that the map \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\Gc_\dl^{-1}: B^{s, s'}_R \to B^{s,s'}_{(1+\eps)R}$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\Gc_\dl^{-1}: B^{s',s}_R \to B^{s',s}_{(1+\eps)R}$ }\DIFaddend is continuous with a continuous inverse $\Gc_\dl: B^{s',s}_{(1-\eps)R} \to B^{s',s}_R$.

\smallskip
\noi {\rm(ii)} The map $\Gc_\dl^{-1}$ is unbounded on $H^s(\R^2)$ for $s< - 1$.


\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
We start with (i). It suffices to check that the quadratic term in \eqref{eq:gauge} is a (small) bilinear map over $B_R$. Supposing, without loss in generality, that $|\xi|\le |\xi_1|\sim |\xi_2|$,
\begin{align*}
&\sup_{\|g\|_{L^2}\le 1} \int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} \jap{\xi}^sK\mathbbm{1}_{A^c_\delta}(\xi_1,\xi_2)\widehat{f}_1(\xi_1)\widehat{f}_2(\xi_2)g(\xi)d\xi_1d\xi \\\lesssim & \sup_{\xi_1} \left(\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} \mathbbm{1}_{A^c_\delta} \frac{\jap{\xi}^{2s}}{\jap{\xi_1}^{2s+2}\jap{\xi_2}^{2s+2}}d\xi\right)^{\frac{1}{2}}\|f_1\|_{H^s}\|f_2\|_{H^s} \lesssim \delta^{2+2s}\|f_1\|_{H^s}\|f_2\|_{H^s},
\end{align*}
and the claim follows from \eqref{eq:escolhadelta}.

To prove (ii), take $\widehat{f}(\xi)=\jap{\xi}^{-1-s-}$. Then, for $|\xi|<1$,
$$
\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} K\ind_{A^c_\dl}(\xi_1,\xi_2)\widehat{f}(\xi_1)\widehat{f}(\xi_2)d\xi_1 \sim \int \frac{1}{\jap{\xi_1}^{4+2s+}}d\xi_1 = \infty,
$$
since $s<-1$.
\end{proof}

\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\simao{For $s=-1$, the gauge transform is still a bounded operator: in dual form, we must prove that
$$
\left|\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} \ind_{A^c}\frac{\widehat{f}(\xi_1)\widehat{f}(\xi_2)\widehat{g}(\xi)}{\jap{\xi}} d\xi_1d\xi\right|\lesssim \|f\|_{L^2}^2\|g\|_{L^2}
$$
which is is a consequence of
$$
\left|\int \jap{\dx}^{-1}h g dx\right|\lesssim \|h\|_{L^1}\|g\|_{L^2},\quad (h=(\mathbf{P}_{>1}f)^2),
$$
and thus reducible to
$$
\|h\|_{L^2(\R^2)}\lesssim \|h\|_{W^{1,1}(\R^2)},
$$
the endpoint of Sobolev embedding (which holds nevertheless). 
}
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{remark}
\DIFadd{At the endpoint $s=-1$ the gauge transform is still a bounded operator on $H^{-1}(\R^2)$: writing the relevant bilinear form in dual variables, the estimate reduces, via Sobolev embedding $W^{1,1}(\R^2)\embeds L^2(\R^2)$, to the standard duality $|\int \jap{\dx}^{-1} h\, g\,dx| \les \|h\|_{L^1}\|g\|_{L^2}$ applied with $h=(\mathbf{P}_{>1} f)^2$.
}\end{remark}
\DIFaddend 

To conclude the proof of Theorem\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend \ref{thm:main_intro}, we proceed via a density argument as in the KdV case\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{~}\DIFaddend \cite{chcora}, which hinges on the following equivalence \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{result}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{between the original and gauged flows at high regularity}\DIFaddend .

\begin{proposition}\label{PRO:equiv}
Let $s' \ge s > -1$ with $s'\gg1$ sufficiently large, $R>0$, $0<\dl \ll R^{-\frac{1}{2s+2}}$, and $u_0$ satisfying
\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{align}
%DIFDELCMD < \label{equiv-0}
%DIFDELCMD < u_0\in H^{s'}(\R)
%DIFDELCMD < \quad
%DIFDELCMD < \text{and}
%DIFDELCMD < \quad
%DIFDELCMD <  \|u_0\|_{H^s}<R.
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align}\label{equiv-0}
u_0\in H^{s'}(\R^2) \quad \text{and} \quad \|u_0\|_{H^s}<R.
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Moreover, let }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{Let }\DIFaddend $u \in X^{s',b}(0,T)$ be the solution to \eqref{eq:NV} with initial data $u_0$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, for some $T>0$, }\DIFdelend constructed in \cite{angelopolous, kazeykinamunoz1, kazeykinamunoz2}, \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{and }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{where $T>0$ is its maximal time of existence, and let }\DIFaddend $z\in X^{s', b}(0,T_{\delta,R})$ be the solution to \eqref{z1} with initial data $z_0 := \Gc_\delta[u_0]$ \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{in }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{provided by }\DIFaddend Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv}. Then \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{, we must have }\DIFdelend $T \ge T_{\delta,R}$ and
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{the following identity holds:
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{align} \label{equiv-1}
%DIFDELCMD < z(t)=\Gc_\delta[u(t)]
%DIFDELCMD < \quad
%DIFDELCMD < \text{in}
%DIFDELCMD < \quad
%DIFDELCMD < C([0,T_{\delta,R}]; H^{s'}(\R^2)).
%DIFDELCMD < \end{align}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \begin{align}\label{equiv-1}
z(t)=\Gc_\delta[u(t)] \quad \text{in} \quad C([0,T_{\delta,R}]; H^{s'}(\R^2)).
\end{align}\DIFaddend 
\end{proposition}

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \begin{proof}[Sketch of the proof] %%%
\DIFdel{As the proof follows exactly as in \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Section 5]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, we just give a brief overview of the key ingredients}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The proof of Proposition~\ref{PRO:equiv} and the deduction of Theorem~\ref{thm:main_intro} from it occupy the remainder of this section.
}

%DIF >  =====================================================================
%DIF >   density.tex --- density argument for Sharp_NV (Theorem 1.1).
%DIF > 
%DIF >   Adapted from §5.2-§5.3 of CC-kdv10.tex (\cite{chcora}). NV-specific
%DIF >   features: (i) $\FL^{s,p}(\R)\rightsquigarrow H^s(\R^2)$, with the
%DIF >   smallness $\dl\ll R^{-1/(2s+2)}$; (ii) the $E$-perturbation in the
%DIF >   linear part of \eqref{eq:NV}; (iii) the multiplier $\Psi_E$ in the
%DIF >   Type~III nonlinear term \eqref{eq:multiplicadores}; (iv) the planar
%DIF >   outer integration costs one extra power of $n$ ($N_0=5$ versus
%DIF >   $N_0=4$ in KdV).
%DIF >  =====================================================================

\DIFadd{The proof of Theorem~\ref{thm:main_intro} is closed by a frequency
truncation/density procedure following \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Section~5]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
; the
NV-specific deviations are listed in the header. The parameters
$s'\ge s>-1$ (with $s'$ eventually large), $R>0$ and
$0<\dl\ll R^{-1/(2s+2)}$ are fixed throughout, so that
\eqref{eq:escolhadelta} holds}\DIFaddend .

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{First, setting $\widehat{\mathbf{P}_nu}(\xi):=\ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi|)\widehat{u}(\xi)$, one considers the
solution $u_n$ of truncated \eqref{eq:NV} equation
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\tag{NV$_n$}\label{eq:NV_n}
%DIFDELCMD < 	\partial_t u + (\partial^3 + \overline{\partial}^3)u + \frac{3}{4}\mathbf{P}_n(\partial(u\overline{\partial}^{-1}\partial u) + \overline{\partial}(u\partial^{-1}\overline{\partial}u)) + E(\overline{\partial}^{-1}\partial^2 u + \partial^{-1}\overline{\partial}^2 u)=0,
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}%%%
\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \subsection{\DIFadd{Truncated dynamics}}

\DIFadd{Given $n\in\N$, write $\mathbf{P}_n$ for the Fourier projector with
symbol $\ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi|)$, $\xi\in\R^2$, and consider the
}\emph{\DIFadd{frequency-truncated Novikov-Veselov equation}}
\begin{equation}\tag{NV$_n$}\label{eq:NV_n_dens}
\dt u_n + (\partial^3+\overline\partial^3) u_n
+ \tfrac34 \mathbf{P}_n\!\left( \partial(u_n\overline\partial^{-1}\partial u_n)
+ \overline\partial(u_n\partial^{-1}\overline\partial u_n) \right)
+ E(\overline\partial^{-1}\partial^2 u_n+\partial^{-1}\overline\partial^2 u_n)=0,
\end{equation}\DIFaddend 
with \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{initial data $u_0\in H^s(\R^2)$. Since the algebraic procedure described in Section\ref{sec:nfe} are independent of $n$, we may also write the corresponding truncated gauged transform via its inverse
}%DIFDELCMD < \begin{equation}\label{eq:gauge_n}
%DIFDELCMD < \mathcal{G}_{\delta,n}^{-1}[f]=f+\F_{z}^{-1}\left(\int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2} K\ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi|)\mathbbm{1}_{A^c_\delta}(\xi_1,\xi_2)\widehat{f}(\xi_1)\widehat{f}(\xi_2)d\xi_1\right),
%DIFDELCMD < \end{equation}
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{and the gauged variable $z_n(t)=\mathcal{G}_{\delta,n}[u_n](t)$ satisfies the corresponding gauged \eqref{eq:NV_n} equation. Observe that Lemma\ref{LEM:D} holds regardless of }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$u_n(0)=u_0\in H^{s'}(\R^2)$. Since $\mathbf{P}_n$ commutes
with the linear group, the resonance set $A$ and the phase
$\Psi=\Psi_0+E\Psi_E$ from Section~\ref{sec:nfe} are insensitive to
the cut-off; consequently the normal-form reduction of that section
carries over to \eqref{eq:NV_n_dens} unchanged. Define
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:Kmul_n}
K_{\bul,n} := K_\bul\, \ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi_\bul|),
\qquad \bul\in\TT^0,
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{the truncated analogue of $K_\bul$ in \eqref{Kmul}, and let
$\Gc_{\dl,n}$ be the }\emph{\DIFadd{truncated gauge transform}} \DIFadd{determined by
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:gauge_n_dens}
\Gc_{\dl,n}^{-1}[f] := f + \F_z^{-1}\!\left( \int_{\xi=\xi_1+\xi_2}
K\,\ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi|)\, \mathbbm{1}_{A^c_\dl}(\xi_1,\xi_2)\,
\widehat f(\xi_1)\widehat f(\xi_2)\, d\xi_1 \right),
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{i.e.\ \eqref{eq:gauge} with the indicator inserted. The conclusions
of Lemma~\ref{LEM:D} hold for $\Gc_{\dl,n}$ with $\dl$, $\eps$, $R$
all uniform in }\DIFaddend $n$. \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{The corresponding }\emph{\DIFadd{truncated gauged
equation}} \DIFadd{is
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:GNV_n_dens}\tag{$\Gc_\dl$-NV$_n$}
\dt z_n + (\partial^3+\overline\partial^3)z_n
+ E(\overline\partial^{-1}\partial^2+\partial^{-1}\overline\partial^2)z_n
= \sum_{j=1}^\infty \sum_{\TT\in\Tr_j}\sum_{\l=1}^5
\Ncal_{\l,n}(\TT;z_n),
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{where $\Ncal_{\l,n}(\TT)$ arises from $\Ncal_\l(\TT)$ in \eqref{z1}
by substituting each $K_\bul$ in \eqref{eq:multiplicadores} with
$K_{\bul,n}$.
}\DIFaddend 

\DIFdelbegin %DIFDELCMD < \smallskip
%DIFDELCMD < %%%
\DIFdel{On the other hand,
the multilinear estimates (Proposition\ref{prop:bourgL2})  are also }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \subsection{\DIFadd{Multilinear estimates with }\texorpdfstring{$n$}{n}\DIFadd{-loss}}

\DIFadd{Since $\ind_{[0,n]}$ only shrinks the multipliers,
Proposition~\ref{prop:bourgL2} transfers verbatim to $\Ncal_{\l,n}$.
The equivalence argument also requires a coarser estimate trading
the gap $s'-s$ for a polynomial factor in $n$ --- the planar version
of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.2]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
.
}

\begin{lemma}\label{lem:dens_estimativas}
\DIFadd{There exists $N_0=N_0(s)\in\N$ (with $N_0=5$ admissible for
$-1<s\le 0$) such that, for $s'\ge s+2$, $j,n\in\N$, $\TT\in\Tr_j$,
$\l\in\{1,\dots,5\}$, $1\le k\le j+1$ and
$f_1,\dots,f_{j+1}\in H^{s'}(\R^2)$,
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:dens_estimativas}
\|\Ncal_{\l,n}(\TT)[f_1,\dots,f_{j+1}]\|_{H^s(\R^2)}
\le n^{N_0}\, C^j\, \|f_k\|_{H^s}
\max_{\substack{1\le k'\le j+1\\ k'\ne k}}\!\left(
\|f_{k'}\|_{H^{s'}}\!\!\!\prod_{\substack{k''\ne k,k'}}\!\!\|f_{k''}\|_{H^s}
\right),
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{for some $C=C(s,\dl)>0$ }\DIFaddend independent of $n$\DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{, $j$ and $\TT$.
}\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\DIFadd{We import the strategy of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.2]{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
and flag the two
NV-specific entries. Combining \eqref{wint0c},
\eqref{eq:multiplicadores} and \eqref{eq:Kmul_n} produces the
pointwise bound
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:mul_n_pointwise}
|\mul_{\l,n}(\TT)(\vec\xi)|
\le C^j\, n\, \max_{\bul\in\TT^\infty}|\xi_\bul|^2\,
\ind_{[0,n]}(|\xi|)
\prod_{\bul\in\TT^\infty}\frac{1}{\jap{\xi_{\bul1}}\jap{\xi_{\bul2}}},
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{in which $|\xi_\bul|\le n$ for $\bul\in\TT^0$ has already been used;
the two derivatives sitting on the largest final frequency are
swallowed by $s'\ge s+2$, exactly as in \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
.
}

\DIFadd{The first NV-specific entry concerns the Type~III multiplier
$\mul_3(\TT)$ of \eqref{eq:multiplicadores}: it carries an extra
$E\Psi_E(\star)$ with $|\Psi_E(\star)|\lesssim|\xi_\star|$
(Section~\ref{sec:multi}). Since the truncation forces
$|\xi_\star|\le n$, this contributes one additional power of $n$
beyond \eqref{eq:mul_n_pointwise}.
}

\DIFadd{The second is dimensional: the outer integration in
\eqref{eq:dens_estimativas} takes place on $\R^2$. Running the
$p=2$ argument of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.2]{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
verbatim ---
Cauchy-Schwarz, then successive integration along the final
subtrees, then the elementary bound
$\int_{|\xi|\le n}d\xi\lesssim n^d$ with $d=2$ in place of $d=1$ ---
yields \eqref{eq:dens_estimativas} with the total loss
$n^{3+d}=n^5$ (three powers from \eqref{eq:mul_n_pointwise} together
with the recursion, one from the Type~III correction, plus $d=2$
from the planar outer integral). The range $s\ge 0$ is reduced to
the previous one via the standard inequality
$\jap{\xi}^s\le j\,\max_{\bul\in\TT^\infty}\jap{\xi_\bul}^s$
of \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.2]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
.
}\end{proof}

\subsection{\DIFadd{High-regularity well-posedness for the truncated gauged equation}}

\DIFadd{Following \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.4]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, we upgrade
Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv} to a uniform-in-$n$ statement and
sharpen uniqueness at the top regularity.
}

\begin{lemma}\label{lem:zn_nv}
\DIFadd{Let $s'\ge s>-1$ with $s'\ge s+2$, $R>0$, and
$0<\dl\ll R^{-1/(2s+2)}$. For every $n\in\N$ and every
$z_{0,n}\in H^{s'}(\R^2)$ with $\|z_{0,n}\|_{H^s}\le R$, there exists
a unique solution $z_n\in X^{s',b}(0,T_{\dl,R})$ to
\eqref{eq:GNV_n_dens} with $z_n(0)=z_{0,n}$, where $T_{\dl,R}$ is
the time from Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv} (independent of $n$).
Moreover, for $t\in[0,T_{\dl,R}]$,
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:bounds_zn_nv}
\|z_n(t)\|_{H^s}\le 2R,
\qquad
\|z_n(t)\|_{H^{s'}}\le 2\|z_{0,n}\|_{H^{s'}},
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{and $z_n$ is unique in
$\{z\in C([0,T_{\dl,R}]; H^{s'}(\R^2)):\,
\|z\|_{L^\infty_t H^s_x}\le 10R\}$.
}\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\DIFadd{The existence portion and the bounds \eqref{eq:bounds_zn_nv} are a
direct consequence of the proof of Proposition~\ref{prop:lwp_rnv}
together with Remark~\ref{remark:persistence}, since
Proposition~\ref{prop:bourgL2} controls $\Ncal_{\l,n}$ with
$n$-independent constants.
}

\DIFadd{For the sharper uniqueness statement, pick two candidates
$z_n,z_n'$ as in the hypothesis, fix $0<T'\le T_{\dl,R}$, and
combine the Duhamel formula with
\eqref{eq:dens_estimativas} to get
}\begin{align*}
\|z_n-z_n'\|_{L^\infty_{T'}H^s_x}
\lesssim T'\, n^{N_0}\,
\big(\|z_n\|_{L^\infty H^{s'}}+\|z_n'\|_{L^\infty H^{s'}}\big)
\,\|z_n-z_n'\|_{L^\infty_{T'}H^s_x}
\sum_{j\ge 0}(CR)^j.
\end{align*}
\DIFadd{Choosing $T'$ small enough --- the threshold depends on $n$ and on
the two $H^{s'}$ norms --- absorbs the right-hand side and gives
$z_n=z_n'$ on $[0,T']$. A finite chain of such intervals covers
$[0,T_{\dl,R}]$}\DIFaddend .
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{By the proof of Proposition \ref{prop:lwp_rnv} (see also Remark \ref{remark:persistence}),
the truncated gauged equation is well-posed in for initial data $z_{0,n}\in H^{s'}(\R)$ }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \end{proof}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Equivalence of the truncated dynamics at high regularity}}

\DIFadd{For smooth data, the next lemma matches \eqref{eq:NV_n_dens} and
\eqref{eq:GNV_n_dens} through $\Gc_{\dl,n}$ on $[0,T_{\dl,R}]$.
}

\begin{lemma}\label{lem:equiv_n_nv}
\DIFadd{Let $s'\gg 1$ be sufficiently large, $R>0$,
$0<\dl\ll R^{-1/(2s+2)}$, and $u_0\in H^{s'}(\R^2)$ }\DIFaddend with
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{$\|z_{0,n}\|_{H^s}<R$, yielding a solution $z'_{n}\in C([0,T_{\delta,R}]; H^{s'}(\R^2))$ with $\|z_{n}'\|_{L^\infty_tH^s}<2R$. Using the truncation of the nonlinearity onto low frequencies, one then proves that $\mathcal{G}_{\delta,n}[u_n]=z_n=z'_n$ in $C([0,T_{\delta,R}]; H^s(\R^2))$ via uniqueness in}\footnote{\DIFdel{This is where the Fourier truncation is necessary, as it lets us prove that the two solutions coincide on intervals of size $\sim T/n$.}}%DIFAUXCMD
\addtocounter{footnote}{-1}%DIFAUXCMD
\DIFdel{$L^\infty_tH^s$.
Notice in particular that this gives
the uniform time-of-existence for the solutions $u_n$, which was not guaranteed by the \eqref{eq:NV} }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{$\|u_0\|_{H^s}<R$. Then, for every $n\in\N$:
}\begin{enumerate}
\item[\textup{\DIFadd{(i)}}] \DIFadd{there is a unique solution
$u_n\in X^{s',b}(0,T_{\dl,R})$ to \eqref{eq:NV_n_dens} on the
}\emph{\DIFadd{uniform}} \DIFadd{interval $[0,T_{\dl,R}]$, satisfying
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:bounds_un}
\|u_n\|_{L^\infty([0,T_{\dl,R}];H^s)}<3R,
\qquad
\|u_n\|_{L^\infty([0,T_{\dl,R}];H^{s'})}<3\|u_0\|_{H^{s'}};
\end{equation}
\item[\textup{\DIFadd{(ii)}}] \DIFadd{if $z_n$ is the solution to
\eqref{eq:GNV_n_dens} furnished by Lemma~\ref{lem:zn_nv} with
$z_{0,n}:=\Gc_{\dl,n}[u_0]$, then
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:equiv_n_nv}
z_n=\Gc_{\dl,n}[u_n]
\quad\text{in}\quad C([0,T_{\dl,R}];H^{s'}(\R^2));
\end{equation}
\item[\textup{\DIFadd{(iii)}}] \DIFadd{$\|u_n\|_{X^{s',b}(0,T_{\dl,R})}\le
C(\|u_0\|_{H^{s'}})$, with $C$ independent of $n$.
}\end{enumerate}
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
\DIFadd{The proof retains the three-step skeleton of
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.5]{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
; we record only the points where the NV
features enter.
}

\smallskip
\noindent\underline{\DIFadd{Step~1 (forward direction).}}\DIFadd{\
Local well-posedness }\DIFaddend at high regularity
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{angelopolous, kazeykinamunoz1, kazeykinamunoz2}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
}\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{angelopolous,kazeykinamunoz1,kazeykinamunoz2} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
produces $u_n$
on a maximal $X^{s',b}_{\mathrm{loc}}$-interval $[0,T_n)$. Put
$T_{0,n}:=\sup\{0<T\le\min(T_{\dl,R},T_n):
\|u_n\|_{L^\infty_T H^s_x}<3R\}$ and let
$v_n(t):=\F_z(U(-t)u_n(t))$. The algebra of
Section~\ref{sec:nfe} sees only $A$ and $\Psi=\Psi_0+E\Psi_E$, both
preserved by $\mathbf{P}_n$, so $v_n$ solves the truncated normal-form
equation, and the four prerequisites (a)-(d) of
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Section~4]{KOY20} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
are in place: $\F_z v_n(\xi)$ is $C^1$ in $t$ and
has rapid decay in $\xi$ (because $s'\gg 1$), while
Lemma~\ref{lem:dens_estimativas}, applied with $n$ fixed, supplies
the summability and convergence of $\NN_n$, $\BB_n$ and $\MM_n$.
The new Type~III term $\Ncal_{3,n}$ inherits the same bound; the
factor $|\Psi_E(\star)|\lesssim|\xi_\star|$ has been incorporated
into \eqref{eq:multiplicadores} once and for all. Setting
$z_n':=\Gc_{\dl,n}[u_n]$, Lemma~\ref{LEM:D} (now read for
$\Gc_{\dl,n}$) yields
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:z'n_a_priori}
z_n'\in C([0,T_{0,n}];H^{s'}(\R^2)),
\qquad
\|z_n'\|_{L^\infty_{T_{0,n}}H^s_x}<(1+\eps)\,3R,
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{and the chain of term-by-term cancellations from
Lemmas~\ref{LEM:wbd}-\ref{LEM:wint}, identical to
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{chcora}}\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
, certifies that $z_n'$ is an integral solution to
\eqref{eq:GNV_n_dens}}\DIFaddend .

\smallskip
\DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{Having shown the
equivalence between the truncated equations at high regularity,
it remains to
prove that, as $n\to \infty$,
$u_n$ converges to }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \noindent\underline{\DIFadd{Step~2 (matching).}}\DIFadd{\
Lemma~\ref{LEM:D} bounds
$\|z_{0,n}\|_{H^s}=\|\Gc_{\dl,n}[u_0]\|_{H^s}\le R/(1-\eps)$, so the
$z_n$ produced by Lemma~\ref{lem:zn_nv} obeys
$\|z_n\|_{L^\infty_{T_{\dl,R}}H^s}\le 2R/(1-\eps)$. Coupled with
\eqref{eq:z'n_a_priori}, the $C_t H^{s'}$ uniqueness clause of
Lemma~\ref{lem:zn_nv} forces $z_n=z_n'$ in $C([0,T_{0,n}];H^{s'})$.
Reading Lemma~\ref{LEM:D} backwards,
}\begin{equation}\label{eq:un_bound_step2}
\|u_n\|_{L^\infty_{T_{0,n}}H^s_x}
\le (1+\eps)\,\|z_n'\|_{L^\infty_{T_{0,n}}H^s_x}
\le \tfrac{2(1+\eps)}{1-\eps}R<3R,
\end{equation}
\DIFadd{provided $\eps$ is chosen small. Continuity together with the
blow-up alternative of
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{angelopolous,kazeykinamunoz1,kazeykinamunoz2} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
upgrades this to
$T_n\ge T_{\dl,R}$ and $T_{0,n}=T_{\dl,R}$; the second half of
\eqref{eq:bounds_un} is its $H^{s'}$ twin.
}

\smallskip
\noindent\underline{\DIFadd{Step~3 ($X^{s',b}$-bound).}}\DIFadd{\
On any sub-interval of length depending only on
$M:=2\|u_0\|_{H^{s'}}$, }\DIFaddend the \DIFdelbegin \DIFdel{\eqref{eq:NV} solution }\DIFdelend \DIFaddbegin \DIFadd{high-regularity well-posedness of
\mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite{angelopolous,kazeykinamunoz1,kazeykinamunoz2} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
gives
$\|u_n\|_{X^{s',b}}\le C(M)$. A deterministic concatenation,
identical to \mbox{%DIFAUXCMD
\cite[Lemma~5.5, Step~3]{chcora} }\hskip0pt%DIFAUXCMD
and powered by
\eqref{eq:bounds_un}, glues these pieces uniformly in $n$ and
delivers (iii).
}\end{proof}

\subsection{\DIFadd{Proof of Proposition~\ref{PRO:equiv}}}
